201 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Rubenstein v. State


NO. 2000-DP-00727-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2005 Miss. LEXIS 789



December 1, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Opinion withdrawn by, On rehearing at Rubenstein v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 424 (Miss., Aug. 10, 2006)
Substituted opinion at, Remanded by, On rehearing at Rubenstein v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 411 (Miss., Aug. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/05/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KEITH STARRETT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Pike County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of murder and capital murder in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19 and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for the capital murder of a child while engaged in the commission of felonious child abuse, the murder of his stepson, who was the child's father, and the murder of the stepson's wife. During his second trial, the jury convicted him on all three murder charges. He was sentenced to death for the capital murder of the child. The supreme court affirmed, stating that testimony admitted by the wife's sister involving an insurance scam with defendant was properly admitted pursuant to Miss. R. Evid. 403, 404(b), and 804(b)(5) because the declarant was unavailable and because the trial court analyzed the five requirements for admission of the hearsay. Those requirements were trustworthiness, materiality, probative value, interests of justice, and notice. Defendant's Confrontation Clause rights were not violated under U.S. Const. amend. VI or Miss. Const. art. III, § 26 because he made no objection at trial that his right was violated. The trial court also determined that the declarant, the wife, was unavailable, and it made an on-the-record examination that the evidence possessed adequate indicia of reliability and particularized guarantees of trustworthiness.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

202 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Lowery


NO. 2004-IA-01849-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


912 So. 2d 461; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 673



October 13, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TISHOMINGO COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/20/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. TALMADGE D. LITTLEJOHN.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee purchaser filed a complaint alleging that an implied easement by necessity existed across a plot of land owned by appellants, three adjoining owners, who filed a motion to dismiss, which was joined by third seller, alleging that the purchaser failed to serve them with process within 120 days as required by Miss. R. Civ. P. 4(h). The Chancery Court of Tishomingo County (Mississippi) denied the motion to dismiss. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The chancellor stated that the purchaser had shown good cause for not serving process on the two owners within the 120-day period of Rule 4(h). The purchaser filed his complaint on January 7, 2004. Rule 4(h) required service of a summons and complaint upon a defendant within 120 days after filing the complaint. Service of the summons on all the owners should have occurred by May 6, 2004. Two of the three owners were never served with process. Even at the time of the hearing on August 20, 2004, neither had ever been served with a summons. Furthermore, the purchaser did not move for an extension of time, nor did he assert good cause as to why service was not timely made. At the hearing, counsel for the purchaser alleged that the reason for not effecting proper service was because of ongoing settlement discussions. However, the two owners were not part of those discussions. The Supreme Court of Mississippi found that the chancellor erred in failing to dismiss the two owners pursuant to Rule 4(h) and 4(e) for failure to serve process as required and that the chancellor abused his discretion in failing to set out specific reasons as to findings of fact in his order or his bench opinion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded with instructions that (1) the chancellor dismiss the case without prejudice as to the two owners and (2) consider anew the motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction filed by the other owner.

 

203 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Yarbrough v. State


NO. 2004-KA-00540-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


911 So. 2d 951; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 610



September 22, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NESHOBA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/11/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the Neshoba County Circuit Court, Mississippi, of the sale of cocaine, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(a)(1) (Rev. 2001). Defendant timely appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a meeting with law enforcement agents, a confidential informant purchased rock cocaine from defendant at defendant's residence. At issue on appeal was whether defendant was denied an impartial jury drawn from a representative cross-section of his community. The State conceded that the black population was a distinctive group within the county. The State correctly pointed out, however, that the proper test was not how many black people actually served on the jury; rather, the proper test was whether the method used to draw the venire led to a fair representation of the black population within the county. The supreme court determined that defendant failed to establish a prima facie showing of a violation of the fair-cross section requirement. Moreover, defendant primarily relied on counsel's argument in his motion, and he failed to show systematic exclusion. Defendant also claimed on appeal that he was improperly denied a mistrial after the admission of certain testimony. The supreme court found that the trial judge did everything he could, short of granting a mistrial, to keep the jury from considering the improper testimony of the witness.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

204 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Powers v. Tiebauer


NO. 2003-CP-01877-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


939 So. 2d 749; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 533



August 25, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NEWTON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/25/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. H. DAVID CLARK, II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a paternity action, the Newton County Chancery Court, Mississippi, adjudicated appellee, the father, as the subject child's natural father. Appellant, the mother, had objected to the father's petition to have the child's surname changed. She had filed a motion to amend the judgment, but she did not act on it. Almost three years later, at a final hearing on paternity, the chancery court held she had abandoned said motion. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The order entered by the chancellor in November 2000 was a final determination as to paternity and the change of the child's surname. The order was "temporary" only as it related to custody, support, and visitation. The final hearing did not occur until July 2003. On appeal, the mother argued that she had a fundamental right, as a mother, to retain the birth name given to her child, and that the paternal presumption in Miss. Code Ann. § 93-9-9(1) constituted both a due process and equal protection violation. First, although other jurisdictions had established that a parent had a fundamental constitutional right in his/her child's name, the state supreme court had not recognized that same was fundamental. Secondly, she had made no challenge to the constitutionality of § 93-9-9(1) in her motion to alter or amend, and the father and the trial court were first apprised of her constitutional challenge when she appealed to the supreme court. Third, the Mississippi Attorney General had received no notice of her constitutional challenge until he received her appellate brief. Thus, the supreme court held the issue abandoned, and also procedurally barred per Miss. R. Civ. P. 24(d).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancery court was affirmed.

In re Extension of the Boundaries of Laurel v. Sharon Waterworks Ass'n


NO. 2003-AN-01368-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


918 So. 2d 1269; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 493



August 11, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Motion granted by In re Extension of the Boundaries of Laurel v. Sharon Waterworks Ass'n, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 70 (Miss., Feb. 2, 2006)
Appeal after remand at City of Laurel v. Sharon Waterworks Ass'n (In re Extension of the Boundaries of the City of Laurel), 2009 Miss. LEXIS 4 (Miss., Jan. 15, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/30/2003. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. B. REEVES, JR.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city filed a complaint in the nature of a petition to ratify and confirm the extension of its boundaries. The senior status judge appointed to hear the case issued a decision that certain legislation was constitutional. The city later amended its complaint. The Second Judicial District of the Chancery Court of Jones County, Mississippi, granted the annexation as to the land as to one area only. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city argued that the annexation met with the indicium of reasonableness and that the chancellor erred in finding that the indicia weakly suggested annexation of a smaller portion of the area. The city argued that the chancellor was correct in his assertion that the city had experienced spillover growth; however, an exhibit demonstrated spillover in all areas of the proposed annexation area, and it was not limited to a certain area. Although the city's population had declined, the city only lost a small amount of people. The city was also 72.4 percent developed. The supreme court found that the chancellor did not issue an order as to his findings and ruling on the issue of whether H.B. 1730, Reg. Sess. (Miss. 1996) violated Miss. Const. § 88. In addition, the supreme court had insufficient information based upon the chancellor's opinion to base its determination. Some of the indicia of reasonableness that the chancery court used was adequate; however, the 12 indicia overall were not detailed enough pursuant to its application to each parcel.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the judgment, and the matter was remanded.

Quitman County v. State


NO. 2003-SA-02658-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


910 So. 2d 1032; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 438



July 21, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Quitman County Miss. v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 636 (Miss., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/7/2003. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: QUITMAN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANN H. LAMAR.
State v. Quitman County, 807 So. 2d 401, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 288 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged the decision of the Quitman County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which entered a judgment for appellees, the State, the governor, and the attorney general (the state), in the county's declaratory action alleging that the State breached its duty to provide effective assistance of counsel in violation of Miss. Const. art. III, § 26.


OVERVIEW: The county alleged that Miss. Code Ann. §§ 25-32-7, and 99-15-17, requiring the counties to provide legal services for indigent criminal defendants, were unconstitutional. The county argued that the circuit judge should have applied the Strickland standard. The court affirmed and held that the county did not present any evidence on any one of the central factual allegations in its complaint and did not try to show specific examples of when the public defenders' legal representation fell below the objective standard of professional reasonableness. It was well established that each county was an agency or subdivision of the State, created for administration and other public purposes. As to expert testimony, the circuit judge allowed opinion testimony as long as there was sufficient background testimony to render the opinion helpful, and her refusal to allow an expert to answer two "ultimate issue" questions was not abuse of discretion. Further, the circuit judge did not treat the testimony of various judges as expert opinion testimony on the issue of whether the public defenders were providing constitutionally adequate representation, so the admission thereof was not erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

 

207 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Green v. Cleary Water, Sewer & Fire Dist.


NO. 2003-CT-01062-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


910 So. 2d 1022; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 394



June 23, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Green v. Cleary Water, Sewer & Fire Dist., 2005 Miss. LEXIS 565 (Miss., Sept. 15, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Green v. Cleary Water, Sewer & Fire Dist., 547 U.S. 1098, 126 S. Ct. 1883, 164 L. Ed. 2d 568, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3287 (2006)
Related proceeding at Green v. Cleary Water, Sewer & Fire Dist., 2009 Miss. LEXIS 430 (Miss., Sept. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/17/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JASON H. FLOYD, JR.
Green v. Cleary Water, Sewer & Fire Dist., 910 So. 2d 1, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 761 (Miss. Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff district residents brought suit seeking a declaration that defendant district's ordinance was invalid and an injunction prohibiting enforcement of that ordinance. Plaintiff-intervenor city sought to intervene. A special chancellor the district summary judgment. A divided Mississippi Court of Appeals affirmed. The residents sought review.


OVERVIEW: The district implemented a wastewater use ordinance that regulated the disposal of wastewater by residents who were not connected to the district's sewer system. The issues presented were distilled down to two: (1) whether the district had the authority to enact its ordinance, and (2) whether summary judgment was properly granted. The residents argued that a water or sewer district, being a statutory creation, could only exercise those powers expressly granted or necessarily implied by the legislature. The district did have authority under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 19-5-173 & -175 to enact an ordinance which would protect its water supply; this action was not preempted by the Mississippi Individual On-Site Wastewater Disposal System Law. Nevertheless, the chancellor erred in granting summary judgment. There was a genuine issue of material fact as to whether the ordinance enacted by the district conflicted with rules and regulations adopted by the Mississippi Department of Health. A determination was required as to whether any of the Department of Health's policies were impacted by the ordinance. Summary judgment was also inappropriate as to the residents' takings argument.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment, and the matter was remanded for additional proceedings.

Jordan v. State


NO. 1999-DR-01391-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


918 So. 2d 636; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 305



May 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jordan v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 459 (Miss., July 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CLARKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/01/1996. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WALTER BAILEY.
Jordan v. Mississippi, 527 U.S. 1059, 144 L. Ed. 2d 829, 120 S. Ct. 26, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 4671 (1999)



DISPOSITION: LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought post-conviction relief from his conviction of two counts of capital murder and the death sentence imposed by the jury in the Clarke County Circuit Court, Mississippi. Petitioner and his counsel raised numerous issues regarding the admission of evidence, the effectiveness of his counsel, constitutional issues, as well as whether petitioner was mentally retarded and entitled to an Atkins hearing.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed he was an unwilling participant in a robbery scheme which resulted in two brutal murders of the victim and his two-year-old son. Petitioner raised claims of error as to his psychiatric exam in the presence of a police officer; the State's disclosure of exculpatory evidence; his counsel's failure to call an expert witness as to which gun fired the fatal shot, to conduct adequate discovery and voir dire, and to request parole eligibility instructions; and the disproportionality and excessiveness of his sentence. The court held that petitioner waived many of the issues by failing to raise them at trial or on direct appeal and was, therefore, barred by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(1) (Supp. 1994). The court rejected petitioner's claim that he was less culpable than the co-participant and that his sentence was disproportionate and excessive because under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-1-3 (Rev. 2000) they were equally culpable for the capital murders where they both conspired to rob and kill the victims, petitioner admitted he fired one shot at the father, and petitioner failed to support his claim of mental retardation that would entitle him to an Atkins hearing.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for post-conviction relief, holding that it found no error requiring vacation of the judgment of conviction and imposition of the death penalty.

Roman Catholic Diocese v. Morrison


NO. 2003-IA-00743-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2003-IA-00744-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


905 So. 2d 1213; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 295; 22 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1531



May 5, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 27, 2005.
Reconsideration denied by Roman Catholic Diocese of Jackson v. Morrison, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 432 (Miss., June 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/31/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/18/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant church administration filed an interlocutory appeal of orders of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which directed defendant to produce requested discovery and denied defendant's motion to dismiss an action by plaintiffs, a mother and three children, for several claims that arose from the alleged sexual molestation of the children by defendant's priest.


OVERVIEW: After the parents learned of allegations of molestation and confronted church officials, the priest was allowed to remain in the parish and continued to abuse children. The court held that enforcing the duty to protect against sexual molestation of children would not excessively entangle the courts in religious matters. The level of authority by defendant over its priests belied any notion that defendant was immune from claims against it under the theory of vicarious liability. There is nothing remotely religious about such reprehensible conduct such as molestation. Plaintiffs' claim of negligent hiring, retention and supervision of the priest was simply a negligence claim. Thus the court found no merit to the assertion that the Free Exercise Clause deprived civil courts of jurisdiction over plaintiffs' complaint. The cloak of religion, which does not shield religious institutions from civil responsibility for fraud or breach of contract, surely could not serve to shield such institutions from civil responsibility for more abhorrent conduct such as sexual molestation of a child. Finally, limited privilege waivers did not serve to waive privilege generally under Miss. R. Evid. 503.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision denying the motion to dismiss and vacated the discovery order, and remanded.

Pub. Emples. Ret. Sys. v. Stamps


NO. 2003-CC-02599-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


898 So. 2d 664; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 255



April 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Public Emples. Ret. Sys. v. Stamps, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 264 (Miss., Apr. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/8/2003. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD. MOTION FOR REHEARING FILED: 02/17/2005.
Public Emples. Ret. Sys. v. Stamps, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 37 (Miss., Jan. 20, 2005)



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: REVERSED AND RENDERED; ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Public Employees' Retirement System (PERS) sought review of an order entered by the Circuit Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County, (Mississippi), which reversed the order of the Board of Trustees of PERS Board. The Board had denied appellee claimant's request for disability benefits. The claimant then appealed to the circuit court and was granted relief. When PERS appealed, the claimant cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was a public school teacher who complained of neck pain and stopped working. Even though medical reports showed great progress and no blanket restrictions on working, the claimant did not return to work. The court concluded that the circuit court erred by reversing the PERS decision to deny the claimant disability benefits because the PERS decision was supported by substantial evidence, was not arbitrary and capricious, was made within the scope or power granted to PERS, and did not violate the claimant's constitutional rights. The court noted that the claimant did not meet her burden to prove to the PERS medical board that she was disabled because although she may have needed her surgery, she was clearly able but unwilling to return to her job as a teacher. The court rejected the claimant's cross-appeal, finding in part that a physician's report challenged by the claimant was not hearsay, even though the report was written by someone not present at the hearing. The court noted that PERS did not have the subpoena powers to compel the report's author to be present. The court determined that there was no denial of due process to the claimant in the PERS proceedings.


OUTCOME: On direct appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, and it rendered judgment reinstating the denial of disability benefits by the PERS Board of Trustees. The court affirmed on cross-appeal.

Webb v. Town Creek Master Water Mgmt. Dist.


NO. 2003-CA-02270-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


903 So. 2d 701; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 236



April 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Webb v. Town Creek Master Water Mgmt. Dist. of Lee, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 428 (Miss., June 30, 2005)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Town Creek Master Water Mgmt. Dist. of Lee v. Webb, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 355 (Miss., July 26, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/13/2003. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WOODROW WILSON BRAND, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the life tenants and remaindermen of a piece of property, sought review of a judgment of the Lee County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which granted the district's motion for summary judgment dismissing the claims against it. The appeal arose from two consolidated cases, an easement condemnation action by the water district and appellants' action against the district for damages and other relief.


OVERVIEW: The filed a petition to acquire a permanent easement on which to construct a water retarding structure. The life tenants and the remaindermen owned the interests in the property. The life tenants were not made parties to the petition. After construction of the dam had begun, both the life tenants and the remaindermen filed a complaint seeking damages for the destruction of their property. On appeal, the two actions were consolidated. The court found that the district failed to follow the clear procedures outlined in Miss. Code Ann. § 51-29-39. Appellants all had an interest in the property, but not one of them were served. Furthermore, the only two individuals who had a present possessory interest in the property were not made parties to the petition. The court concluded that the trial court erred in holding that no notice was required to appellants. It also found that the failure to give notice and to join all interested parties was a denial of due process. Finally, the court determined that the trial court needed to determine on remand the amount of compensation to be awarded to appellants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for further proceedings, including the determination of the amount of compensation to be awarded to the life tenants.

 

212 of 603 DOCUMENTS


City of Starkville v. 4-County Elec. Power Ass'n


NO. 2004-CA-00577-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


909 So. 2d 1094; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 189



March 24, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/20/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT L. LANCASTER.
City of Starkville v. 4-County Elec. Power Ass'n, 819 So. 2d 1216, 2002 Miss. LEXIS 1 (Miss., 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision of the Oktibbeha County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which dismissed its complaint, holding that the city's right to purchase appellee power company's service rights created under a 1963 Service Area Agreement was non-existent due to the city's failure to seasonably petition the Mississippi Public Service Commission (MPSC) for approval of its contract.


OVERVIEW: In 1963, the city and power company entered into a service area agreement. The 1956 Public Utilities Act was amended in 1987 under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 77-3-13, 77-3-17, and 17-3-21, and H.B. 997 clarified the amendments. The court held: (1) the chancellor erred in his finding that the city lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of H.B. 997, but the error was harmless; (2) In granting partial summary judgment, the chancellor correctly interpreted and applied H. B. 997 as expressly clarifying the intended legislative interpretation to be given to the amendments to §§ 77-3-13, -17 & -21; (3) the chancellor appropriately granted partial summary judgment pending the city's petition to the MPSC for approval of its proposed purchase of the power company's service rights and distribution facilities within an annexed area in accordance with the 1963 Agreement; (4) the chancellor did not err in finding that H.B. 997 did not violate the Contracts Clause of the federal and state constitutions because the regulation of the state's public utilities fell within the legislature's authority, and inasmuch as the city failed to secure MPSC approval, its contractual rights had not vested.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

213 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Knox v. State


NO. 2002-DR-00912-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


901 So. 2d 1257; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 190



March 24, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Knox v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 357 (Miss., June 2, 2005)
Clarified by Knox v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 340 (Miss., June 2, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Knox v. Mississippi, 546 U.S. 1063, 126 S. Ct. 797, 163 L. Ed. 2d 630, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 9080 (2005)
Stay granted by Knox v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 99 (Miss., Feb. 3, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: AMITE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/29/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR.
Knox v. State, 805 So. 2d 527, 2002 Miss. LEXIS 24 (Miss., 2002)



DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of capital murder in the Amite County Circuit Court (Mississippi) and sentenced to death for the victim's murder. On direct appeal, the supreme court affirmed the inmate's conviction and death sentence. The inmate subsequently filed his petition for post-conviction relief and supplement/amendment to the petition for post-conviction relief. The State filed its response. The inmate filed his rebuttal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that his attorneys were ineffective for failing to pursue a Batson claim. However, the trial court found that some of the State's reasons for striking African-American jurors were a close call but accepted them and allowed the challenges to stand. Additionally, the supreme court found that the inmate did not show that a different outcome would have resulted had the Batson objections been sustained. Thus, the inmate's attorneys were not ineffective on that issue. Also, the inmate's attorneys were not ineffective because they (1) filed numerous pre-trial motions; (2) cross-examined nine out of 11 prosecution witnesses; (3) ultimately decided not to call a witness because he would have corroborated the State's witnesses; and (4) one of them met with him on numerous occasions and even discussed a plea offer from the State with him, which the inmate ultimately rejected. In addition, the accusation that trial counsel failed to properly investigate was merely an unfounded allegation. Further, in the capital murder case, the evidence was sufficient to find the inmate guilty of the underlying offense of robbery because he killed the victim and took her house and car keys.


OUTCOME: The supreme court denied the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

214 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Lawrence County Sch. Dist. v. Bowden


NO. 2004-CC-00556-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


912 So. 2d 898; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 173



March 17, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Bowden v. Lawrence County Sch. Dist., 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 48 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAWRENCE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/21/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. J. LARRY BUFFINGTON.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lawrence County Chancery Court, Mississippi, dismissed appellant guidance counselor's appeal for lack of jurisdiction, finding that the statutes authorizing appeals to the chancery court from school board decisions, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 37-9-101 to 37-9-113 (Rev. 2001), were unconstitutional. The counselor and appellee school district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The chancery could held sua sponte that the Education Employment Procedures Law, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 37-9-101 to 37-9-113, unconstitutionally conferred jurisdiction to the chancery court. Both parties argued that the chancellor incorrectly held that the statutes were unconstitutional. The appellate court found that in light of the fact that neither of the parties raised the constitutionality of Mississippi's Education Employment Procedures Law, the chancellor exceeded his powers in raising the issue sua sponte. Appeals of state board and agency decisions generally fell under the constitutional purview of "matters in equity." Review of board and agency decisions (and, in particular, school board decisions) fell under the scope of those matters in equity which the Mississippi Constitution permitted chancery courts to hear. The chancellor erred in concluding otherwise.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for the purpose of reviewing whether the decision not to renew the counselor's contract was supported by substantial evidence, was arbitrary and capricious, was beyond the power of the administrative agency to make, or was in violation of the counselor's statutory or constitutional rights.

 

215 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Jordan v. State


NO. 2002-DR-00896-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


912 So. 2d 800; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 170



March 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jordan v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 344 (Miss., June 2, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/24/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KOSTA N. VLAHOS.
Jordan v. State, 786 So. 2d 987, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 109 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of murder. Following multiple appellate proceedings, defendant was sentenced to death. After the affirmation of that sentence on appeal, defendant filed an application for leave to proceed in the trial court and a petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant abducted the victim from her home, forcing her to leave her three-year-old son sleeping alone in the house, and forced her to drive to a wooded area. Defendant shot the victim in the back of the head, returned to town, and continued with his plan to extort money from the victim's husband. For two days defendant led the husband to believe that his wife was alive and well. Defendant was captured by the police when he attempted to pickup the ransom money. On appeal, the court found that (1) many of defendant's arguments had been rejected before in prior proceedings and were barred by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21; (2) the trial court did not err in allowing an officer's expert testimony as to blood spatters; (3) there was sufficient proof of aggravating circumstances to support defendant's death sentence under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-105(5)(b) (Rev. 2000); (4) defendant failed to show ineffective assistance of counsel regarding preparation for an expert witness, objecting to the jury instructions, and regarding a mental evaluation of defendant; and (5) there was sufficient evidence for the jury to find that the murder was heinous, atrocious, cruel, conscienceless, and pitiless.


OUTCOME: Defendant's application for leave to seek post-conviction relief was denied.

Hodges v. State


NO. 2002-DP-00337-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


912 So. 2d 730; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 164



March 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hodges v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 350 (Miss., June 9, 2005)
Motion granted by Hodges v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 405 (Miss., June 23, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hodges v. Mississippi, 126 S. Ct. 739, 163 L. Ed. 2d 579, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 8670 (U.S., 2005)
Motion denied by Hodges v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 813 (Miss., Dec. 15, 2005)
Motion granted by, Remanded by Hodges v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 214 (Miss., Apr. 20, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hodges v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 692 (Miss., Dec. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/13/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN M. MONTGOMERY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Lowndes Circuit Court (Mississippi) that convicted him of capital murder pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e) and of kidnapping his ex-girlfriend, and that sentenced him to death based on the finding that he killed his ex-girlfriend's brother during the commission of burglary, a felony. Defendant was sentenced to a term of 20 years for the kidnaping conviction and his motion for a new trial was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised numerous claims of error, including ineffective assistance of counsel, jury instruction errors, a defective indictment, improperly admitted evidence of other crimes and photographs, and the jury's consideration of an invalid aggravator. The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction for the underlying crime of burglary, where the evidence showed he broke into his girlfriend's home with the intent to kill her. Also the kidnapping conviction was supported by evidence that showed the girlfriend did no go with defendant voluntarily. The court found that the "avoiding lawful arrest" aggravating circumstance was properly submitted to the jury because the evidence showed that defendant killed the girlfriend's brother in an attempt to conceal his identity or to "cover his tracks." The court found that the capital murder indictment sufficiently specified the underlying burglary felony and that defendant was not entitled to a manslaughter instruction. Also any error in the admission of prior bad act evidence was harmless and the photograph of the murder victim was not unduly gruesome.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Le v. State


NO. 2002-DP-01855-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


913 So. 2d 913; 2005 Miss. LEXIS 151



March 3, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 28, 2005.
Motion to strike denied by Le v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 152 (Miss., Mar. 3, 2005)
Motion denied by, Motion to strike denied by Le v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 153 (Miss., Mar. 3, 2005)
Motion granted by Le v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 154 (Miss., Mar. 3, 2005)
Motion to strike denied by Le v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 155 (Miss., Mar. 3, 2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion granted by Le v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 409 (Miss., June 23, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Thong Le v. Mississippi, 546 U.S. 1004, 126 S. Ct. 622, 163 L. Ed. 2d 508, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 8254 (2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion denied by Knox v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 263 (Miss., May 20, 2010)
Motion dismissed by Le v. State, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 181 (Miss., Apr. 3, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/23/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES W. BACKSTROM.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder and imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant participated in the beating death of several victims. The co-defendant committed suicide prior to trial. Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death. In affirming, the court determined that the decision whether or not to conduct a sequestered voir dire was within the discretion of the trial court. The court rejected defendant's argument that the jury did not reflect a fair cross-section of the community under the Sixth Amendment since the jury was not required to mirror the community. Further, defendant's Batson challenge failed because the State gave race-neutral reasons for using its peremptory challenges. Defendant's statement was admissible, despite the fact that his religion was used by police, because it was only mentioned after defendant had partially confessed. Further, the evidence showed that defendant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his right to remain silent. Even if the prosecution failed to disclose expert testimony under Miss. Unif. Cir. & County Ct. Prac. R. 9.04, the evidence of blunt force trauma was merely cumulative. Finally, the imposition of the death penalty under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101 (Rev. 2000) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Public Emples. Ret. Sys. v. Stamps


NO. 2003-CC-02599-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2005 Miss. LEXIS 37



January 20, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Public Emples. Ret. Sys. v. Stamps, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 171 (Miss., Mar. 9, 2005)
Motion to strike granted by Public Emples. Ret. Sys. v. Stamps, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 262 (Miss., Apr. 14, 2005)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Public Emples. Ret. Sys. v. Stamps, 898 So. 2d 664, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 255 (Miss., Apr. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/8/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD.



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: REVERSED AND RENDERED; ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Public Employees' Retirement System (PERS) appealed from an order entered by the Circuit Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County, Mississippi, reversing the order of the Board of Trustees of the Public Employees' Retirement System (PERS Board) which denied appellee employee's claim for disability benefits. The employee then appealed to the circuit court and was granted relief. PERS appealed, and the employee cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a teacher for over 27 years before she ended her career. The question was whether her claim met the statutory requirements for the receipt of disability benefits. The circuit court reversed the PERS Board's decision denying benefits, determining that it was not supported by substantial evidence. However, on appeal, the court held that the PERS Board's decision was supported by substantial evidence, was not arbitrary and capricious, was made within the PERS Board's scope or power, and did not violate the employee's constitutional rights. The employee failed to meet her burden of proving she was in fact disabled. Though she might have needed her surgery, she was clearly able but unwilling to return to her job. The record clearly supported the PERS Board's order, which took into consideration all of the medical evidence, which did not establish that the employee's ailments were disabling. She was capable of performing her work duties from a medical standpoint; therefore, she was not entitled to disability benefits from the State of Mississippi. The trial court impermissibly reweighed the evidence and substituted its judgment for that of the administrative agency.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed on direct appeal and judgment was rendered reinstating the denial of disability benefits by the PERS Board. The judgment was affirmed on cross-appeal.

 

219 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Long v. McKinney


NO. 2003-IA-00849-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


897 So. 2d 160; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1404



December 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Long v. McKinney, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 246 (Miss., Apr. 7, 2005)
Related proceeding at Long v. Mem'l Hosp. at Gulfport, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 570 (Miss., Oct. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/19/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY O. TERRY, SR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death suit, appellants, relatives of decedent, appealed the judgment of the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which refused to consolidate their suit with that of appellee, decedent's daughter, which was filed one day prior.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that the trial court erred by failing to consolidate their suit with that of appellee. The supreme court agreed. All claims for the wrongful death of a person had to be litigated in the same suit and in the same court. Because appellee engaged counsel and filed a wrongful death suit without participation of the personal representative or appellants, she did so as the representative of all statutory beneficiaries and must, within a reasonable time following the filing of the complaint, provide reasonable notice to all other wrongful death beneficiaries, to the personal representative of the decedent, if one has been appointed, and to each person who bore a relationship to the deceased specified in Miss. Code Ann. § 11-7-13. Because appellee's attorney filed the first suit on behalf of all wrongful death beneficiaries, all such beneficiaries should have received notice of the litigation. Because there was no conflict of interest between appellee and the estate, and as the estate, through appellee as administratrix, employed a law firm to represent the estate, that firm should have represented the estate also.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

220 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Maranatha Faith Ctr., Inc. v. Colonial Trust Co.


NO. 2003-CA-02349-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


904 So. 2d 1004; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1405



December 2, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/17/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT L. LANCASTER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee insurer levied execution on certain personal property found on appellant church's premises and on the church's chose in action against a third party after a judgment entered in favor of the insurer remained unsatisfied. The church moved to quash execution of the writ, and the Lowndes County Chancery Court, Mississippi, denied the motions. The church appealed.


OVERVIEW: The church appealed the trial court's ruling and argued that a levy of execution upon a chose of action was not authorized by Mississippi law. Further, the church argued to the trial court that a writ of execution based on a judgment lien may only be applied to the proceeds of a lawsuit and not the lawsuit itself. The appellate court affirmed the denial of the church's motion to quash the writs of execution. The appellate court held that a reasonable interpretation of Miss. Code Ann. § 11-7-7 (Rev. 2004) was that a chose in action could be transferred to the same extent as other property and therefore treated the same as other property. The appellate court noted that the Legislature did not choose to limit § 11-7-7. Accordingly, save any statutory exceptions, there was no limitation on the execution of a chose in action. Further, Miss. Code Ann. § 13-3-135 implicitly authorized that a chose in action could be sold under writ of execution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

221 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Mayor of Clinton v. Welch


NO. 2003-CC-02103-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


888 So. 2d 416; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1412



December 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 20, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/23/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. TOMIE T. GREEN.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a mayor and city board of aldermen (the City), sought reversal of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) allowing appellee property owners to keep a tree house in their front yard, claiming that the tree house violated Clinton, Miss., Zoning Ordinance § 401.05, which was in force at the time the owners began construction of the tree house.


OVERVIEW: According to the owners, the City's building inspector and zoning official approved the project and indicated that no permit was required. The court noted that the ordinance, as it applied to front yards, prohibited "accessory buildings" and prohibited "uses." However, the definition within the ordinance was of an "accessory structure or use," which was defined as a detached structure. The City provided no notice to the public that it utilized the definition of "accessory structure or use" to define "accessory building or use." The court held that the § 401.05 of the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and that the application of the definition of "use" to § 401.05 was unconstitutionally vague. Further, the doctrine of laches applied and also equitable estoppel, because the City sat by in silence while the owners invested thousands of dollars in reliance on the approval while the treehouse was being built over a five-year period. Finally, the court found that the City violated Clinton, Miss., Zoning Ordinance § 2411.03, which stated, that only in case of a tie vote could an application be forwarded to the mayor and aldermen board without recommendation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Hughes v. State


NO. 2000-DR-00051-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


892 So. 2d 203; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1355



November 10, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Hughes v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1370 (Miss., Nov. 10, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hughes v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1365 (Miss., Nov. 10, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hughes v. Mississippi, 545 U.S. 1130, 125 S. Ct. 2935, 162 L. Ed. 2d 870, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 4906 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/20/1996. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GEORGE C. CARLSON, JR.
Hughes v. State, 735 So. 2d 238, 1999 Miss. LEXIS 131 (Miss., 1999)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO FILE PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed an application for leave to seek post-conviction collateral relief in the Tate County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted the inmate of kidnapping, rape and murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held: (1) because the pathologist's testimony was not paramount to the case, defense counsel was not professionally negligent in failing to seek an independent expert in pathology; (2) since the venue had already been affirmed and held proper, trial counsel was not deficient in failing to successfully challenge the choice of venue; (3) because a potential alibi witness could not recall which day he saw the inmate, trial counsel was not ineffective for not calling him; (4) the inmate was not mentally retarded and the decision to have him testify was regarded as strategic; (5) the inmate's prior rape conviction was one of violence sufficient to be used as an aggravating circumstance pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(5)(b) (Rev. 2000); (6) there was nothing in the affidavits of family that seemed likely to have changed the outcome at sentencing; (7) the inmate signed a written consent regarding DNA samples; (8) the evidence overwhelmingly belied the assertions that the inmate was mentally retarded; and (8) a brief exposure to jurors of the inmate in handcuffs was not inherently prejudicial as to require a mistrial.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's application for postconviction relief.

Thorson v. State


NO. 2002-DP-01420-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 96-DP-00144-SCT, NO. 90-DP-00015-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


895 So. 2d 85; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1350



November 4, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Thorson v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 83 (Miss., Feb. 3, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Thorson v. Mississippi, 546 U.S. 831, 126 S. Ct. 53, 163 L. Ed. 2d 83, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 6177 (2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Thorson v. State, 994 So. 2d 707, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 497 (Miss., 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Thorson v. State, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 451 (Miss., Sept. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/08/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY O. TERRY, SR.
Thorson v. State, 721 So. 2d 590, 1998 Miss. LEXIS 392 (Miss., 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of the Second Judicial District of Harrison County (Mississippi), which convicted defendant of capital murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant cited 33 assignments of error. The court affirmed and held, among other things, (1) an "avoiding arrest" aggravator was properly submitted, as defendant threw items into the woods; (2) the jury's decision was unambiguous; (3) the "especially heinous" aggravator existed, because the victim was left to bleed to death in her car and then he shot her; (4) two cases from other states did not apply, because Mississippi's capital scheme was distinct; (5) the trial court did not commit error regarding the jury instructions; (6) the State's "send a message" appeal to the jury in closing arguments complied with Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(1); (7) the State did not err in commenting on defendant's lack of remorse; (8) because there were no reversible errors in any part, there was no reversible error to the whole case; (9) there was no evidence supporting a finding that the death sentence was imposed under the influence of passion; (10) defendant waived the issue of the jury's composition, as he made no objection to the seating of the jury; (11) photographs of the victim's body had probative value; and (12) defendant had no right to counsel during his mental evaluation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Noxubee County Sch. Dist. v. United Nat'l Ins. Co.


NO. 2003-CA-00936-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


883 So. 2d 1159; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1202; 10 Wage & Hour Cas. 2d (BNA) 967; 150 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P34,923



September 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Noxubee County Sch. Dist. v. United Nat'l Ins. Co., 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1244 (Miss., Sept. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NOXUBEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/7/2003 TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES T. KITCHENS, JR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured sought review of the decision of the Noxubee County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, insurer and claims adjuster, in the insured's action after coverage was denied.


OVERVIEW: The action involved an insurance dispute between the insurer and insured, a school district, with the central issue bearing on coverage and the applicability of an exclusionary clause. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the insurer and claims adjuster, and the court affirmed. Because the insured's failure to comply with the Fair Labor Standards Act, 29 U.S.C.S. § 201 et seq., in a manner that exposed it to liability for overtime compensation was neither a "wrongful act" nor a "wrongful employment act" within the meaning of the school board policy, the trial court did not err in granting summary judgment in favor of the insurer and claims adjuster. Further, Exclusion 12 of the school board policy specifically excluded claims brought against the insured regarding back wages, overtime, or future wages. The exclusion was clear and unambiguous and was therefore enforced according to its terms. A thorough review of the record revealed no evidence of bad faith by the insurer and claims adjuster in denying the insured's request for coverage. Therefore, the trial court's grant of summary judgment was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gray v. State


NO. 1999-DR-00592-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


887 So. 2d 158; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1166



September 16, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gray v. Mississippi, 545 U.S. 1130, 125 S. Ct. 2935, 162 L. Ed. 2d 870, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 4905 (2005)
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Motion denied by Gray v. Epps, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33943 (S.D. Miss., May 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NEWTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 1/25/1996. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON.
Gray v. State, 728 So. 2d 36, 1998 Miss. LEXIS 371 (Miss., 1998)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of capital murder by the Newton County Circuit Court, Mississippi. His conviction was upheld on direct appeal. He sought leave to pursue post-conviction relief, asserting numerous instances of ineffective assistance of counsel, particularly in regard to jury selection and counsels' alleged failure to mitigating evidence at sentencing. He also asserted the death penalty in his case constituted cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: The evidence established that petitioner accosted a 79-year-old woman and later raped and murdered her. Petitioner asserted counsel failed to properly argue a motion for change of venue. However, counsel had submitted a motion and affidavits alleging defendant could not receive a fair trial in the county because defendant was black and the victim was white. On direct appeal, the instant court had found the motion was properly denied. As with several issues petitioner raised, the matter was barred from further review. The instant court also held: (1) petitioner failed to establish a prima facie case of systematic exclusion under the standard set out in Lanier and same prevented him from demonstrating that his trial counsel's performance was deficient under the first prong of the Strickland standard; (2) counsel did, in fact, present a case in mitigation for the jury to consider and he was given a mental assessment showing that he was not as mentally retarded, thus, counsel was not ineffective at the sentencing phase, and (3) the jury instructions given at the sentencing phase, in accordance with Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(7), did not violate petitioner's Eighth Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The application for leave to file a petition for post-conviction relief in the trial court filed by petitioner was denied.

Mitchell v. State


NO. 2002-DR-00479-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


886 So. 2d 704; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1037



August 19, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Mitchell v. Mississippi, 544 U.S. 1022, 125 S. Ct. 1982, 161 L. Ed. 2d 864, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 3824 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/24/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KOSTA N. VLAHOS.
Mitchell v. State, 792 So. 2d 192, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 76 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Harrison County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of capital murder committed while being under a sentence of life in prison. He was sentenced to death by lethal objection. Defendant filed an application for leave to seek post-conviction relief in the trial court, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that trial counsel failed to present mitigating evidence during the sentencing phase of trial as to mental retardation. The appellate court noted that there was no evidence to suggest that defendant was mentally retarded. The appellate court previously held that it was reasonable to conclude that there was sufficient evidence that the murder was committed in an effort to avoid lawful arrest. The issue was procedurally barred from further consideration on collateral review by the doctrine of res judicata. Defendant's allegations as to a motion for a change of venue, failure to secure a speedy trial, and demand for jury questionnaires were without merit. Defendant was not entitled to formal notice in the indictment of the aggravating circumstances to be employed by the prosecution, and an indictment for capital murder put defendant on notice that the statutory aggravating factors would be used against him. The appellate court previously considered and rejected the issue of police trespass and whether the trial court erred in not instructing the jury on the lesser-included offense of manslaughter. Defendant's other issues were without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

227 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. State


NO. 2003-KA-00313-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


881 So. 2d 820; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1011



August 5, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 8, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 1/30/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GEORGE B. READY.
Walker v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1006 (Miss., Aug. 5, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The DeSoto County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted defendant of possession of two or more precursor chemicals (pseudoephedrine and lithium), knowing that the precursor chemicals would be used to unlawfully manufacture a controlled substance (methamphetamine), pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-313(1)(a)(ii) (Supp. 2003). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The store where defendant purchased the material called the police. Defendant's argument that an ordinary person buying a box of decongestant would not know they were committing a crime failed. Under mens rea, defendant must have known or should have reasonably have known that the decongestant would be used in the manufacture of a controlled substance. Defendant claimed probable cause and/or reasonable suspicion did not exist because the first officer on the scene began following his truck before he was able to determine that defendant's appearance matched that of the description given. Probable cause was not needed to watch the truck because of defective brake lights, follow the vehicle after matching defendant's description with that given by a store employee, and make an investigatory stop. All that was needed for these activities was reasonable suspicion. Because defendant's truck violated Miss. Code Ann. § 63-7-13(3), and a traffic violation had occurred, stopping the truck was reasonable. Because the investigatory stop was based on a reasonable suspicion, after the ephedrine was seen in plain view, the officers had probable cause to search the vehicle.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bishop v. State


NO. 2002-DR-00932-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


882 So. 2d 135; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 773



July 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Bishop v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 828 (Miss., July 1, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Bishop v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1295 (Miss., Sept. 23, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bishop v. Mississippi, 543 U.S. 1189, 125 S. Ct. 1401, 161 L. Ed. 2d 194, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2123 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Bishop v. Epps, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60321 (N.D. Miss., Aug. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/04/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK A. RUSSELL.
Bishop v. State, 812 So. 2d 934, 2002 Miss. LEXIS 39 (Miss., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's motion for leave to proceed in trial court with petition for post-conviction relief denied. Motion to strike exhibits and appendices to, and portions of, petitioner's reply brief is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed a motion for leave to proceed in the trial court with a petition for post-conviction relief. The prisoner had been convicted of the crime of capital murder, with the underlying felony of kidnapping, and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner provided the actual killer with the hammer used on the victim, kicked the victim, chased the victim, and held him down while the lethal blows were being inflicted. The court rejected the prisoner's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel. Although counsel failed to move for a change of venue, each of the impaneled jury members affirmatively stated that they could serve as fair and impartial jurors. The record also revealed overwhelming evidence of the prisoner's guilt. Because defense counsel acted in accord with the prisoner's specific instructions not to present mitigation evidence, their performance was not deficient. The prisoner's actions overwhelmingly showed that he evinced a reckless indifference to the victim's killing because he was an aggressor and willfully imposed great danger upon the victim. His involvement in the crime was sufficient to justify the death sentence. The proof in the record did not support the prisoner's claim of being mentally retarded as to require remand to the trial court for an Atkins hearing. The prisoner supported his claim with copies of school records and affidavits of family members, none of which were sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court denied the prisoner's motion for leave to proceed in the trial court with a petition for post-conviction relief. The court granted the State's motion to strike.

 

229 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Felder v. State


NO. 2002-CP-00325-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


876 So. 2d 372; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 776



July 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Felder v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 835 (Miss., July 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/04/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MIKE SMITH.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to manslaughter in the Pike County Circuit Court, Mississippi. Defendant was sentenced to 20 years in prison and a $ 10,000 fine. He was also ordered to pay a $ 10,000 assessment into the crime victims' compensation fund. Defendant moved for post-conviction relief, asserting that his plea was involuntary, that his plea counsel was ineffective, and that his sentence was excessive. His motion was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Based on a review of the plea colloquy, it was clear that defendant understood the consequences of his guilty plea and understood the maximum penalty. It was also clear that he was competent and that his plea was voluntarily and intelligently made. Furthermore, defendant had expressed satisfaction with his attorney's representation. Thus, defendant's arguments that his plea was involuntary and that he was denied effective assistance were rejected. However, under the general manslaughter penalty statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-25 (Rev. 2000), defendant could have been fined "or" he could have been sentenced to 20 years in the penitentiary, but not both. However, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-32(1) provided that offenses punishable by imprisonment in the state penitentiary for more than one year and for which no fine was provided elsewhere by statute, could be punishable by a fine not in excess of $ 10,000. Thus, while the fine provision of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-25 (Rev. 2000) was not applicable, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-32(1) was applicable and it allowed for the trial court's imposition of the subject fine. The $ 10,000 assessment to the crime victims' compensation fund was also proper.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. However, as to the amount defendant was assessed for the crime victims' compensation fund, because there was a discrepancy between the amount reflected in the transcript and the subsequent sentencing order, the matter was remanded for the limited purpose of clarifying that amount.

 

230 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Univ. of Miss. Med. Ctr. v. Robinson


NO. 2003-IA-00152-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


876 So. 2d 337; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 778



July 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Univ. of Miss. Med. Ctr. v. Robinson, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 807 (Miss., July 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 1/8/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. TOMIE T. GREEN.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, mother and child, sued defendant medical center for injuries the child sustained during a medical procedure. The Hinds County Circuit Court, Mississippi, denied the medical center's summary judgment motion and held that Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(4) (Rev. 2002) tolled the minor's claim. The medical center appealed and alleged the 2002 amendment to § 11-46-11(4) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The child was burned during a surgical procedure in 1995. The mother had retained an attorney by 1996, but no action was filed until January 2002 which was well past the one-year statute of limitations in the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11 (Rev. 2002). The mother claimed that the March 2002 amendment to § 11-46-11(4) allowed the claim to be filed pursuant to the minor's savings clause. The appellate court noted that under Miss. Const. art. 4, § 97, the legislature could not enact any legislation that would revive a claim that had previously been barred by a statute of limitations. Under the 2002 amendment to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(4), the legislature held that any claim from April 1, 1993 on was subject to a savings clause that tolled the claim until the minor was 21. As the amendment revived the minor's claim that had been barred by the statute of limitations, the 2002 amendment to § 11-46-11(4) was unconstitutional to the extent that it makes the savings clause applicable to all claims since April 1, 1993. The state supreme court did hold that the 2000 amendment to § 11-46-11(4), that enacted a savings clause in April 2000 was valid and enforceable.


OUTCOME: The denial of the medical center's summary judgment was reversed, and judgment was rendered in favor of the medical center. Plaintiffs' complaint was dismissed.

Miss. Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. Osborne


NO. 2003-JP-00057-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


876 So. 2d 324; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 780



July 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Miss. Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. Osborne, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 824 (Miss., July 1, 2004)
Later proceeding at Miss. Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. Osborne, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 823 (Miss., July 1, 2004)
Related proceeding at Miss. Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. Osborne, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 9 (Miss., Feb. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COMMISSION ON JUDICIAL PERFORMANCE. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 2/25/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PATRICIA D. WISE.
Miss. Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. Osborne, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 748 (Miss., Jan. 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: PUBLIC REPRIMAND; INTERIM SUSPENSION RESCINDED AND JUDGE OSBORNE REINSTATED TO OFFICE; AND ASSESSED THE COSTS OF THIS PROCEEDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge appealed a decision by the Mississippi Commission on Judicial Performance that ordered that the judge be publicly reprimanded, and that his temporary suspension be rescinded and he be reinstated to office. The judge was also ordered to pay the costs of the proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The judge was a county court judge and was appointed to office in August 2001 and later elected to a full term. The judge admitted that between October 2001 and January 2002, he filed on behalf of clients, five complaints in chancery courts, one complaint in circuit court, and two petitions in bankruptcy court. The commission filed a complaint against the judge in January 2003 and alleged the judge had continued to practice law after his appointment to the bench, thereby violating Miss. Code Ann. §§ 9-1-25 and 9-9-9, as well as Miss. Code Jud. Conduct Canons 1, 2A, 2B, 3A and 4G. The judge claimed that he had relied on the language of Miss. Code Ann. § 9-9-9, and claimed the term "pending cases" was not limited to cases pending in court. The state supreme court agreed that the term "pending cases" was somewhat ambiguous, but that filing new actions in no way constituted concluding cases actually pending. However, the court also noted that as the judge did not wilfully abuse the privilege of filing new complaints while in office, the court adopted the commission's recommendation that the judge be publicly reprimanded and that he be reinstated after his temporary suspension.


OUTCOME: The commission's findings and recommendations were adopted.

 

232 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Miss. Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. Wilkerson


NO. 2002-JP-02105-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


876 So. 2d 1006; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 796



July 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Miss. Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. Wilkerson, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 816 (Miss., July 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WICH APPEALED: COMMISSION ON JUDICIAL PERFORMANCE. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/13/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. C. E. MORGAN, III.



DISPOSITION: Commission's complaint and case dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Mississippi Commission on Judicial Performance recommended that appellee judge be sanctioned for extra-judicial public statements of his views on the rights of gays and lesbians. The issue was whether the judge's right to send a letter to the editor of his local weekly newspaper and to make statements over a telephone to a reporter from a radio network were protected by U.S. Const. amend. I and Miss. Const. art. III, § 13.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court pointed out that the letter pre-dated Miss. Code Jud. Conduct Canon 4(A)(1) and could not have been subject to it. Only Miss. Code Jud. Conduct Canon 2(A) could apply to the letter. Gay rights was a political/public issue, and, in the absence of a compelling state interest, no sanction could have been imposed. The court also concluded that the judge's statements were protected religious speech. Canon 2(A) constituted a prior restraint on the judge's right to publicly state his political and religious views, and the Commission had not met its burden of showing a compelling governmental interest. Because the court was convinced that the statements made by the judge constituted religious and political/public issue speech specially protected by U.S. Const. amend. I, and because the court was further persuaded that in some cases, including the case sub judice, forced concealment of views on political/public issues served to further no compelling governmental, public, or judicial interest, the court was compelled to reject the recommendation of the Commission. The court held that, under the particular facts of the case, sanctions were constitutionally impermissible.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the Commission's complaint and the case with prejudice.

 

233 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Berry v. State


NO. 2002-DR-00301-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


882 So. 2d 157; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 802



July 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 13, 2004.
Reported at Berry v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 840 (Miss., July 1, 2004)
Motion denied by Berry v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 841 (Miss., July 1, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Berry v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1207 (Miss., Sept. 30, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Berry v. Mississippi, 544 U.S. 950, 125 S. Ct. 1694, 161 L. Ed. 2d 528, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2822 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 6/25/1992. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN.
Berry v. State, 802 So. 2d 1033, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 255 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO FILE PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought leave to file a petition for post-conviction relief from a judgment of the Chickasaw County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder for kidnapping and murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant claimed that he was entitled to relief based on cumulative errors, and his indictment was unconstitutional because it failed to specify the aggravating factors used to sentence him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he was entitled to relief based on ineffective assistance of counsel, the withholding of exculpatory evidence, his mental retardation, improper sentencing instructions, and the indictment failed to state the aggravating circumstances. The court found that there was substantial evidence to support the sentence based on the aggravating factors, including the fact that the murder was committed during the course of a kidnapping, and defendant was a habitual offender. The court rejected defendant's claims of ineffective counsel, finding he failed to show how his counsel's performance and strategy deprived him of a fair trial, and many of the issues were procedurally barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21 (2000) as they were or should have been raised on direct appeal. The court rejected defendant's claim that the aggravating factors elevating the charge to a capital offense must have been included in the indictment. The United States Supreme Court had not found that state capital defendants had a constitutional right to have all aggravating circumstances listed in their indictments. The court noted that the indictment did include the aggravating factors.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's application for leave to file a petition for post-conviction relief.

Grayson v. State


NO. 2002-DR-00588-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


879 So. 2d 1008; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 721



June 24, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Grayson v. Mississippi, 543 U.S. 1155, 125 S. Ct. 1301, 161 L. Ed. 2d 122, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 1593 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GEORGE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/8/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON.
Grayson v. State, 806 So. 2d 241, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 303 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Petition for Post-Conviction Relief and Supplement/Amendment to Petition for Post-Conviction Relief denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief, as well as a supplement/amendment to that petition. Defendant had been convicted of capital murder during the commission of a burglary, and he was sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that he was at the scene of the crime and that he killed the victim. After his conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal, he sought post-conviction relief. The court allowed defendant to supplement his petition, which asserted six additional grounds for relief beyond the initial six from the original petition. The court initially determined that issues relating to suppression of his confession had been previously litigated and were barred by res judicata and by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(3). His counsel was not ineffective in failing to present mitigating evidence, as such was pursuant to defendant's explicit instructions that he preferred the death penalty over life imprisonment. Defense counsel's performance with respect to a change of venue, testing of DNA samples, and a continuance was not deficient. Defendant's sentence was neither disproportionate nor unconstitutional, and the jury's verdict was proper. The aggravating factors were supportive of the jury's verdict, the death sentence was to be carried out upon exhaustion of appeals, regardless of other sentences, and cumulative errors did not require reversal due to cumulative prejudicial effect.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.
