Scott v. State


NO. 1999-DP-00317-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


878 So. 2d 933; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 650



June 10, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Scott v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1022 (Miss., Aug. 12, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Post-conviction relief granted at, in part Scott v. State, 938 So. 2d 1233, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 534 (Miss., Oct. 5, 2006)
Post-conviction proceeding at Scott v. State, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 516 (Miss., Oct. 29, 2009)
Post-conviction proceeding at Scott v. Mississippi, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 617 (Miss., Nov. 21, 2013)
Post-conviction relief granted at State v. Scott, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 222 (Miss., June 1, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/23/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KENNETH L. THOMAS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: BOLIVAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.
Scott v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 666 (Miss., June 10, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Bolivar County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by failing to strike four jurors because they stated that they could not conform their conduct to the law and would automatically return a verdict of death. The supreme court disagreed. The trial court did not err by denying strikes for cause on the jurors. The prospective jurors all stated that they could follow the law and weigh the evidence and mitigating and aggravating factors before making a determination of whether defendant should receive the death penalty. The record was full of questions from the trial court, the State, and the defense concerning the death penalty. The four jurors in question also appeared in the trial judge's chambers and were questioned more extensively by the trial court, prosecution and defense. The record reflected that the defense individually questioned each of the four jurors in chambers. The trial judge placed no restrictions on the attorneys' questions in chambers. Lastly, none of the jurors ever sat on the final impaneled jury, and thus, never even voted on the issue of defendant's guilt or whether he should receive a death or life sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Branch v. State


NO. 2002-DP-01315-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


882 So. 2d 36; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 586



May 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Branch v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 599 (Miss., May 27, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Branch v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1217 (Miss., Sept. 30, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Branch v. Mississippi, 544 U.S. 907, 125 S. Ct. 1595, 161 L. Ed. 2d 282, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2289 (2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at Branch v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 519 (Miss., June 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CARROLL COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/23/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. C. E. MORGAN, III. DISTRICT ATTORNEY: .



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Carroll County Circuit Court (Mississippi) found defendant guilty of capital murder. The jury imposed the death penalty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made a statement to police that he and co-defendant discussed robbing the victim. Later, at the victim's home, they struck her in the head outside her home, defendant held her down so that he could get money out of her pockets, and then they searched her house for more money. They left with about $ 200 and a pistol. The appellate court found that defendant had not made a prima facie showing that he was mentally retarded; therefore, the State was not prohibited by the Eighth Amendment from executing him. Additionally, the appellate court found that defense counsel did not render ineffective assistance during either the punishment or guilt phase of defendant's trial. Furthermore, the jury instructions were appropriate, as they were in accordance with Mississippi law and they fairly and adequately instructed the jury. In addition, the evidence included the testimony of the witnesses who saw defendant and co-defendant together throughout the evening, the blood evidence, the items found at co-defendant's home, and defendant's confession. Thus, reasonable, fair-minded jurors could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of robbery and capital murder.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Puckett v. State


NO. 2000-DR-01077-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI

Rehearing denied by Puckett v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1057 (Miss., Aug. 19, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Puckett v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1058 (Miss., Aug. 19, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Puckett v. Mississippi, 544 U.S. 924, 125 S. Ct. 1638, 161 L. Ed. 2d 483, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2506 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by Puckett v. Epps, 615 F. Supp. 2d 494, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 26433 (S.D. Miss., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/7/1996. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD W. MCKENZIE. DISTRICT ATTORNEY.
Puckett v. State, 788 So. 2d 752, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 168 (Miss., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate filed a petition for post-conviction relief after he was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was indicted in 1996 for the capital murder of the victim while engaged in the commission of the crime of sexual battery in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e). The jury found him guilty of capital murder and imposed a death sentence. He currently filed a petition for post-conviction relief in the supreme court and the supreme court denied the petition. The inmate argued that he was denied due process pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 13-5-1 because one of the jurors could not comprehend English. The supreme court stated that the issue was procedurally barred from being raised for the first time in his petition for post-conviction relief pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(1). However, his contention was also without merit because the record indicated that the inmate affirmed the juror's presence after fully exploring her abilities to read, write, and comprehend English. He was also not denied any constitutional or fundamental rights by the admission of the testimony of the victim's children because their testimony corroborated portions of the victim's husband's testimony. The inmate also offered nothing by way of proof that his defense counsel was ineffective.


OUTCOME: The supreme court denied the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief.

Smith v. State


NO. 1999-DR-01394-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


877 So. 2d 369; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 547



May 20, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Smith v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 551 (Miss., May 20, 2004)
Motion dismissed by, Moot Smith v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 541 (Miss., May 20, 2004)
Later proceeding at Smith v. State, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 519 (Miss., Oct. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/1/1993. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS.
Smith v. State, 729 So. 2d 1191, 1998 Miss. LEXIS 590 (Miss., 1998)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF GRANTED IN PART AND DENIED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought leave to seek post-conviction relief in the trial court in a petition filed against appellee State on the issue of mental retardation, among other issues. The court had previously remanded the post-conviction proceedings to the trial court for the appointment of qualified counsel to represent the inmate, and counsel filed the documents at issue presently before the court.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. He raised various issues in his application for post-conviction relief. The court found most the issues to be without merit. In addition, the court noted that several of the inmate's issues had been raised on direct appeal and had been found to be without merit, and thus those issues were procedurally barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(2). The court rejected the inmate's numerous claims of ineffective assistance of counsel. The court found no error in the attorneys' failure to object to the inmate being shackled at trial because no juror had stated that the shacking affected the conviction. The attorneys were not required to object to sentencing instructions that were proper, nor were the attorneys ineffective for failing to object to the exclusion of certain jurors, given that they did not meet the qualifications of Miss. Code Ann. § 13-5-1 (Rev. 2002). The court did find, however, that it could not, given recent case law, constitutionally deny the inmate an opportunity to present the issue of his possible mental retardation to the trial court. Thus, the inmate's motion for relief was granted to this extent.


OUTCOME: The court granted the inmate leave to proceed in the trial court on the sole issue of his alleged mental retardation. All other claims in his petition for post-conviction relief were denied.

Bell v. State


NO. 1999-DR-01287-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


879 So. 2d 423; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 543



May 20, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Bell v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 537 (Miss., May 20, 2004)
Costs and fees proceeding at, Application granted by, Motion granted by Bell v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 538 (Miss., May 20, 2004)
Reconsideration denied by Bell v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 540 (Miss., May 20, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Bell v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1056 (Miss., Aug. 19, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bell v. Mississippi, 543 U.S. 1155, 125 S. Ct. 1301, 161 L. Ed. 2d 122, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 1594 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GRENADA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/27/1993. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES C. SUMNER.
Bell v. State, 725 So. 2d 836, 1998 Miss. LEXIS 305 (Miss., 1998)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO FILE PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED. PRO SE PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. On direct appeal, his conviction and sentence were affirmed. The inmate filed a petition for post-conviction relief in the Grenada County Circuit Court, Mississippi, and claimed that he received ineffective assistance from counsel, which rendered both the guilt and sentencing phases of the trial unconstitutional. The petition was denied, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the inmate raised a number of arguments to support his claim that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The state supreme court rejected all of the inmate's claims. The state supreme court held: (1) the inmate's counsel was not ineffective just because he was trying three death penalty cases at once and the counsel had sufficient experience, (2) the trial counsel's request for investigation funds was timely, (3) the failure to secure a ballistics expert did not prejudice the inmate, (4) the counsel's choice of whether to call certain witnesses fell within the ambit of trial strategy and did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel, (5) the inmate provided no legal support for his claim that his counsel's failure to request jury questionnaires in addition to the jury summons was ineffective representation, (6) as the counsel's decision not to raise Batson challenges to the State's peremptory challenges was tactical, it was not ineffective representation, and (7) the inmate failed to show that certain jurors could be rehabilitated to consider the death penalty. The inmate's remaining claims were also rejected, and the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The denial of the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

Brawner v. State


NO. 2002-DP-00615-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


872 So. 2d 1; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 458



April 29, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Brawner v. State, 947 So. 2d 254, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 625 (Miss., 2006)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Knox v. State, 75 So. 3d 1030, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 576 (Miss., 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at Brawner v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 364 (Miss., May 24, 2012)
Motion granted by Brawner v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 269 (Miss., May 31, 2012)
Post-conviction relief denied at Brawner v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 274 (Miss., May 31, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/12/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER.
Brawner v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 456 (Miss., Apr. 29, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Tate County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which found him guilty of four counts of capital murder and sentenced him to death, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(f) (Rev. 2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered his ex-wife, her two parents, and his three-year-old daughter. He was indicted on four counts of capital murder. Count one was for the willful murder of his daughter while engaged in the commission of the crime of felonious abuse and/or battery of the child, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-39 (Rev. 2000). The remaining counts were the willful murder while engaged in the commission of the crime of robbery. He was found guilty and sentenced to death. The supreme court affirmed, stating that the trial court did not err in denying his motion to sever count one of the indictment, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-7-1 (Rev. 2000). The killings occurred within a few hours and were all part of the common scheme to rob his ex-father-in-law and eliminate any witnesses. Additionally, the murders were interwoven, and all of the murders occurred at the same place and closely in time. Further, defendant testified at trial that he killed his child because she could identify him. Although the State struck substantially more women than men, the fact that the selected jury incorporated a proportionally larger percentage of women than were in the venire contradicted his claim of gender discrimination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Martin v. State


NO. 2002-KA-00400-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


871 So. 2d 693; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 416



April 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/01/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES W. BACKSTROM.
Martin v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 429 (Miss., Apr. 22, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Mississippi), which convicted him of the murder of his wife and sentenced him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that defendant was competent to stand trial. The court further held that the finding of the trial court regarding defendant's ability to voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently waive his rights and make two separate statements was not clearly erroneous or against the overwhelming weight of the evidence. The trial court was correct in denying defendant's motion to preclude all mentions of the victim's body by applying the rationale that the sheriff's department would have discovered the information given by defendant in his second statement, which was admitted into evidence. Finally, the court found that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-139(1)(a) (Rev. 2000) was not violative of defendant's due process and equal protection rights by specifying criteria to consider in determining which inmates could or could not be considered for earned time allowance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

242 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Barbour v. Delta Corr. Facility Auth.


NO. 2002-CA-01510-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


871 So. 2d 703; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 411



April 22, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 6, 2004.
Reported at Barbour v. Delta Corr. Facility Auth., 2004 Miss. LEXIS 421 (Miss., Apr. 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/3/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM G. WILLARD, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Governor of Mississippi (Governor) and the Mississippi Department of Corrections, sought review of an order from the LeFlore County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which found that the Governor's partial veto of a prison funding bill violated Miss. Const. art. 4, § 73. In an action brought by appellee prison, the court held that the bill was a valid law in its entirety.


OVERVIEW: The Governor approved two sections of a bill that addressed funding for prisons. The Governor vetoed the third section of the bill. Consequently, the prison filed a motion for a temporary restraining order to enjoin the Mississippi Department of Corrections and the Governor from closing its facility. The trial court found that the partial veto violated Miss. Const. art. 4, § 73. The trial court held that the bill was a valid law in its entirety. On appeal, the court found that the third section of the bill was but a condition of the first two sections, which appropriated the funds by the Mississippi Legislature. The language of the bill made the third section reliant upon the first two sections. The Governor's veto could not inhibit the legislative intent of the bill, nor could his veto create new legislation. The court held that the Governor's partial veto of the bill was an unconstitutional veto of a condition of an appropriation bill as written and was a nullity. The trial court properly found that the veto was a nullity and that the bill became law in its entirety in the form passed by the Mississippi Legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Holland v. State


NO. 1999-DR-00273-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


878 So. 2d 1; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 413



April 22, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Holland v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 433 (Miss., Apr. 22, 2004)
Motion denied by Holland v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 436 (Miss., Apr. 22, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Holland v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 997 (Miss., Aug. 5, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Holland v. Mississippi, 544 U.S. 906, 125 S. Ct. 1590, 161 L. Ed. 2d 280, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2273 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/02/1993. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KOSTA N. VLAHOS.
Holland v. State, 705 So. 2d 307, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 388 (Miss., 1997)



DISPOSITION: LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed an application for leave to file a petition for post-conviction relief after the death sentence was imposed for the offenses of murder and rape.


OVERVIEW: The inmate allegedly raped and killed a teenager. Afterwards, he asked a friend to help dispose of the body. After he was convicted and sentenced to death, the case was remanded for resentencing. However, the death penalty was again imposed in the second sentencing hearing. After the sentence was affirmed on review, the inmate filed a petition for leave to file for post-conviction relief. In denying the application, the court determined that the inmate was unable to show that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant failed to show that another expert would have disputed the finding of the State's expert. Further, defense counsel objected to the admission of photographs and the admission of a pathologist's testimony. In addition, the inmate failed to show how other medical records would have persuaded a jury to exercise leniency during sentencing. The court noted that many of the inmate's claims were procedurally barred from collateral review under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(3) because they had been previously litigated. Finally, the court determined that the State was not required to list the aggravating factors in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The application for post-conviction collateral relief was denied.

E. Miss. State Hosp. v. Callens


NO. 2000-CT-00258-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


892 So. 2d 800; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 361; 21 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1162



April 15, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at E. Miss. State Hosp. v. Callens, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 392 (Miss., Apr. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/26/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. L. BRELAND HILBURN.
E. State Hosp. v. Callens, 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 531 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 18, 2001)



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEALS REVERSED. JUDGMENT OF THE CIRCUIT COURT OF THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HINDS COUNTY AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On writ of certiorari, plaintiff, a former state employee, sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Mississippi), which reversed the trial court's judgment in the employee's favor in a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against defendants, state agencies and individual state employees, for retaliatory termination arising from the exercise of his First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, right to speak out on matters of public concern.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who worked at a state hospital, wrote a letter critical of abusive practices and sent it to a state official who was the superior of the hospital's director. The employee's immediate supervisor was highly critical of the employee for having gone over the heads of his immediate superiors. Four days later, the employee was fired. Because he was a probationary employee, his administrative appeal was dismissed. The employee failed to appeal the dismissal order and instead brought suit, alleging retaliation for the exercise of his freedom of speech and wrongful termination. A jury found in his favor, but the court of appeals ruled that the grievance procedure was his exclusive remedy. The court reversed the appellate decision, holding that a retaliatory discharge claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 could be brought against state officials in their personal or individual capacities. The complaint sufficiently identified, as required by Miss. R. Civ. P. 9(a), the individuals against whom § 1983 relief was sought. Qualified immunity did not apply because the employee's speech was on a matter of public concern. Substantial evidence supported the verdict in the employee's favor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the federal civil rights judgment against the director individually but reversed and rendered as to all other defendants. The court affirmed the state law judgment against the agencies but reversed and rendered as to the director and his superior. The court affirmed the award of fees and costs, except as to the director's superior, and found no error in the trial court's refusal to submit the issue of punitive damages.

 

245 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Dycus v. State


NO. 1998-DP-01094-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


875 So. 2d 140; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 366



April 15, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Dycus v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 396 (Miss., Apr. 15, 2004)
Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Dycus v. Mississippi, 161 L. Ed. 2d 271, 125 S. Ct. 1589, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2212 (U.S., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: BOLIVAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 6/19/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KENNETH L. THOMAS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Bolivar County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which, in a jury trial, convicted defendant of capital murder and auto theft and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: The victim, an elderly woman, was beaten and fatally shot during a robbery committed by defendant, who was 17 years old, and his brother. The court found no error in the trial court's decision to strike a juror who was ambivalent as to whether she could impose the death penalty, while refusing to strike a juror who had attended church with the victim's sister. Disqualification of an illiterate juror under Miss. Code Ann. § 13-5-1 did not violate defendant's right to an impartial jury. The trial court did not abuse its discretion when it admitted the alleged murder weapon into evidence and permitted a forensic expert to testify that the victim was shot with the same type of weapon. Photographs of the body were also relevant to establishing the type of weapon. Intent did not have to be proven under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e) because the murder occurred during a robbery. Sufficient evidence supported a finding of aggravating circumstances under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(5). A death sentence for a minor was not cruel or unusual punishment. The prosecution's use in closing argument of biblical imagery and references to the victim's age and frailty constituted fair comment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

Columbia Land Dev., LLC v. Sec'y of State


NO. 2002-CA-02025-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


868 So. 2d 1006; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 286



March 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Columbia Land Dev., LLC v. Sec'y of Miss., 2004 Miss. LEXIS 311 (Miss., Mar. 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/14/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS WRIGHT TEEL.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Mississippi Gaming Commission had conditionally approved a site for gaming, but appellee Secretary of State disapproved the proposed public trust tidelands lease. Appellant property owners challenged the disapproval by filing a petition for declaratory action and mandatory injunction in the Harrison County Chancery Court (Mississippi). The chancery court denied the petition and the subsequent motion for reconsideration. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Despite the approval from the Gaming Commission, the Secretary of State denied the public trust tidelands lease and stated that the site did not satisfy the geographical requirements of the Mississippi Gaming Control Act of 1990, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 75-76-1 et seq. (2000). A trial was held, and the chancery court denied the owners' requested relief and dismissed the petition for declaratory and injunctive relief. On appeal, the court determined that the crucial issue was whether the Secretary of State had the final decision-making authority concerning a proposed public trust tidelands lease. The court held that Miss. Code Ann. § 29-1-107(2) (2000) unequivocally afforded the Secretary of State the discretion to enter into a lease of the public tidelands and that the Secretary of State had the responsibility of preserving the public trust tidelands for the people of the State of Mississippi. The court affirmed the chancery court's judgment, finding that the Secretary of State's decision to deny the lease to the owners was made within the discretion granted to him. The court also reaffirmed the constitutionality of the Public Trust Tidelands Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

247 of 603 DOCUMENTS


PHE, Inc. v. State


NO. 2003-CA-00456-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


877 So. 2d 1244; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 269



March 18, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/7/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM HALE SINGLETARY.
PHE, Inc. v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 275 (Miss., Mar. 18, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff vendors and plaintiff users brought suit against defendant state, before the Hinds County Chancery Court, Mississippi, seeking a declaratory judgment that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-105 (Rev. 2000) violated Miss. Const. art. 3 §§ 13, 14 and 32. The state moved for summary judgment, which was granted. The vendors and users appealed.


OVERVIEW: The vendors and users sold and used sexual devices. They argued, on appeal, that the right to privacy encompassed sexual devices. Nevertheless, the supreme court determined that there was no independent fundamental right of access to purchase sexual devices. Other courts had compared the purchase of sexual devices to the right of access to contraceptives. The supreme court, however, concluded that society's interest in protecting the right to control conception was of greater magnitude than the interest in protecting the right to purchase sexual devices. The vendors next argued that the prohibition on the advertisement, sale, and distribution of sexual devices violated the constitutional right to free speech. The vendors did not question the state's constitutional power to regulate businesses that sell and/or distribute sexual devices. The supreme court determined that the prohibition on the sale and/or distribution of sexual devices constituted only an incidental restriction on the vendors alleged right to freedom of speech that was no greater than was essential to the furtherance of the State's governmental interests.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Cockrell v. Pearl River Valley Water Supply Dist.


NO. 2002-CA-02090-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


865 So. 2d 357; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 69



February 5, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Cockrell v. Pearl River Valley Water Supply Dist., 2004 Miss. LEXIS 172 (Miss., Feb. 5, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/19/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM E. CHAPMAN, III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an alleged harassment victim, sued appellee water supply district, because its employee allegedly hugged and kissed her after arresting her. The Rankin County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granted summary judgment to the district under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (MTCA), Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 et seq., finding that the employee had not acted within the course and scope of his employment. The victim appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who worked as a security patrol officer with the district, arrested appellant for suspicion of driving under the influence of alcohol; during the course of the arrest, he hugged and kissed her without her consent. She argued that, as the employee's acts, though improper, were not criminal, the trial court erred by dismissing her claims against the district. The supreme court did not reach this argument, because it found that the employee's tortious acts were not done to further any purpose of his employer. As the employee had not been acting within the scope of his employment with the district when he hugged and kissed appellant, her claims against the district were barred by Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-7. Appellant's failure to raise the issue of the constitutionality of Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-13 (2002) of the MTCA before the trial court and to notify the Mississippi Attorney General of this pursuant to Miss. R. Civ. P. 24(d) resulted in a procedural bar on this issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Simmons v. State


NO. 2002-DR-00196-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


869 So. 2d 995; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 49



January 29, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Simmons v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 63 (Miss., Jan. 29, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Simmons v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 428 (Miss., Apr. 22, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Simmons v. Mississippi, 543 U.S. 960, 125 S. Ct. 436, 160 L. Ed. 2d 325, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7185 (2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Simmons v. State, 942 So. 2d 802, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 652 (Miss., 2006)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Knox v. State, 75 So. 3d 1030, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 576 (Miss., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/02/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILL JONES.
Simmons v. State, 805 So. 2d 452, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 316 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The inmate filed a motion for leave to proceed in the trial court on a petition for post-conviction relief after his conviction for capital murder and death sentence were affirmed on appeal. He was also convicted of rape and kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death for the murder of the victim. He was also convicted of the rape and kidnapping of the victim's female companion. The supreme court previously affirmed defendant's convictions and he filed a motion for leave to proceed in the trial court with a petition for post-conviction relief. The court denied the motion, stating that the exclusion of the inmate's videotape showing remorse for his actions was proper because his current argument was barred by res judicata. Further, his claim for ineffective assistance of counsel was without merit because he offered no evidence that supported his claim that his trial counsel should have investigated more thoroughly or in certain areas. His death sentence was not disproportionate because the jury found that defendant intended the victim's death and contemplated that lethal force would be used. Ample evidence also showed that defendant actively planned and participated in the robbery and murder. His indictment was not unconstitutional for failure to include and specify the aggravating factors because there was no constitutional right to have the factors listed.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's request relief.

In re Extension & Enlarging of the Boundaries of Laurel


NO. 2002-AN-01805-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


863 So. 2d 968; 2004 Miss. LEXIS 17



January 15, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In the Matter of the Extension & Enlarging of the Boundaries of the City of Laurel, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 24 (Miss., Jan. 15, 2004)
Appeal after remand at In re Extension & Enlarging of Boundaries of the City of Laurel, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 101 (Miss., Mar. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/22/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANKLIN C. McKENZIE, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision from the Jones County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which denied the city's petition to annex certain property without conducting an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: The city sought to annex certain property under Miss. Code Ann. § 21-1-27 (Rev. 2000). In order to annex the property in question, the city also had to annex a right-of-way in order to make it both adjacent and contiguous to the city limits. It filed a petition seeking approval of the annexation in the chancery court. However, without hearing any evidence regarding the annexation's reasonableness, a chancellor stated that the annexation could not have proceeded. After the petition was dismissed, the city sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the chancellor had the duty to determine the reasonableness of the city's proposal under Miss. Code Ann. § 21-1-33 (2001). The chancellor was required to conduct a full hearing allowing for evidence and testimony and utilizing the indicia of reasonableness factors to determine if the proposed annexation was allowed. The court noted that the annexation statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 21-1-27 (Rev. 2000), was not unconstitutionally vague because the reasonableness test was not included in the statute's language. Because a hearing was not conducted, a reversal of the case was required.


OUTCOME: The decision of the chancery court was reversed. The case was remanded with instructions to proceed on the merits with a full hearing to determine whether the proposed annexation was reasonable.

Husband v. State


NO. 2015-KA-00558-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


204 So. 3d 353; 2016 Miss. App. LEXIS 472



July 26, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Husband v. State, 2016 Miss. App. LEXIS 759 (Miss. Ct. App., Nov. 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/04/2015. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PRENTISS GREENE HARRELL. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF MANSLAUGHTER AND SENTENCED TO TWENTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS, WITH TEN YEARS SUSPENDED, AND TO PAY A $5,000 FINE AND $2,500 IN RESTITUTION.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case where defendant was convicted of manslaughter under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-35 (Rev. 2006), the trial court committed reversible error in giving a castle-doctrine jury instruction favoring the victim because a castle-doctrine instruction had never been given in regard to the victim being granted the mandatory rebuttable presumption in Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-15(3) (Rev. 2014) that a person was entitled to use whatever force was necessary to meet or repel an attack from another person, and such an instruction was patently inappropriate as the statute clearly indicated that the rebuttable presumption was granted to a defendant, not the victim; and a reasonable juror could have interpreted the challenged instruction to create a presumption that lessened the State's burden of proof and required rebuttal evidence from defendant to overcome the presumption.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded.

Morgan v. State


NO. 2015-CP-00530-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


193 So. 3d 703; 2016 Miss. App. LEXIS 385



June 14, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/09/2015. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROGER T. CLARK. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DENIED MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF AND REFUSED TO AUTHORIZE FOR PAROLE ELIGIBILITY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court's denial of defendant's request for a parole recommendation was an appealable judgment. HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court's denial of defendant's request for a parole recommendation was not an appealable order. Therefore, the appellate court did not address the merits of the claim; [2]-Although defendant argued that his thirteen-and-a-half-year sentence for transfer of a controlled substance was illegal because it exceeded the new statutory maximum of eight years as set by recent amendments to the sentencing scheme found in Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(b)(1) (Supp. 2015), at the time of defendant's crime and sentencing, the statute provided for a penalty of up to thirty years for transfer of the controlled substance. Thus, defendant's thirteen-and-a-half-year sentence was well within the thirty years permitted by law and was not illegal.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

259 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Barnett-Phillips v. State


NO. 2015-CA-00252-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


195 So. 3d 226; 2016 Miss. App. LEXIS 377



June 14, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/16/2015. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM E. CHAPMAN III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-When Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139, under which defendant was sentenced, was amended, the amendment did not entitle her to the post-conviction relief of being resentenced under the amended statute because her sentence had become final when the statute was amended, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-1 said that, for a sentencing statute to be retroactive, the statute had to so state, and Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139 did not, and Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-33 had no bearing, since her conviction became final before Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139 was amended; [2]-Defendant was not entitled to relief when the trial court declined to recommend to the Parole Board that she be deemed parole eligible because Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3 gave the trial court discretion to issue such a recommendation, and this denial did not implicate an appealable judgment.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: JURY VERDICT AGAINST APPELLANTS/CROSS-APPELLEES FOR $1,500,000 IN ECONOMIC DAMAGES, AND $2,000,000 IN NONECONOMIC DAMAGES, REDUCED TO $500,000 IN ACCORDANCE WITH STATUTORY DAMAGES CAP.

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred when it denied the motion for an IME, because the complaint was sufficient to meet the "in controversy" requirement in Miss. R. Civ. P. 35, there was a reason to find good cause for an IME since the patient's medical records only covered about six months, and there was no medical professional who could testify as a fact or expert witness as to the patient's medical condition and permanent injury; [2]-The trial court erred in admitting an expert's testimony on the patient's permanent physical impairment, because the expert did not reexamine the patient at his final point of healing, rendering his opinion unreliable; [3]-The evidence did not support award of economic damages, because the patient's mother only presented evidence of medical expenses and the testimony on lost wages was based on an unreliable opinion on the patient's permanent impairment.

Brown v. Waldron

COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly granted summary judgment in favor of the sole member of a limited liability company (LLC) in homeowners' action alleging negligence and breach of warranty because the member was not personally liable for the defects in their home under the New Home Warranty Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 83-58-3(a) (Rev. 2011); [2]-The LLC was the builder of the home, not the member; [3]-The member was not acting as the agent of an undisclosed principal because although the member signed the "Notice to Home Buyer of the New Home Warranty Act," all other documents in the record indicated that the LLC was the builder; [4]-The LLC was not reinstated under Miss. Code Ann. § 79-29-825(3) (Rev. 2013) for the sole purpose of evading liability because it was reinstated after the homeowners filed their complaint.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


187 So. 3d 635; 2015 Miss. App. LEXIS 276



May 19, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc McKnight v. State, 2015 Miss. App. LEXIS 548 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 27, 2015)
Writ of certiorari denied McKnight v. State, 186 So. 3d 854, 2016 Miss. LEXIS 142 (Miss., Mar. 31, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/21/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DAVID H. STRONG JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF COUNT ONE, MURDER, AND COUNT TWO, POSSESSION OF A FIREARM BY A CONVICTED FELON, AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER ON BOTH COUNTS TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT THE POSSIBILITY OF PROBATION, PAROLE, OR EARLY RELEASE, WITH THE SENTENCES TO RUN CONSECUTIVELY, AND TO PAY FINES IN THE AMOUNT OF $10,000 ON COUNT ONE, AND $1,000 ON COUNT TWO, AND $6,000 IN RESTITUTION.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court did not err in denying defendant's motion to dismiss for lack of a speedy trial because the State bore no responsibility for any of the delays, defendant filed a motion to dismiss a week before his trial, instead of filing a motion demanding a speedy trial, and defendant's defense was not impaired as a result of the delay; [2]-A witness's testimony that the victim had an issue with defendant's son and appeared to be afraid was permissible under Miss. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant's guilty plea was involuntary because he was affirmatively misinformed by his counsel that he would be eligible for parole on two enhanced counts. HOLDINGS: [1]-To the extent defendant claimed that he would not be paroled on an interstate removal of a child charge, his claims were without merit. Vaughn v. Public Emples. Ret. Sys. of Miss.


NO. 2013-CC-01179-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


182 So. 3d 446; 2015 Miss. App. LEXIS 62



February 10, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Vaughn v. Public Employees' Ret. Sys., 2015 Miss. App. LEXIS 325 (Miss. Ct. App., June 9, 2015)
Writ of certiorari granted Vaughn v. Public Emples. Ret. Sys. of Miss., 2015 Miss. LEXIS 424 (Miss., Aug. 13, 2015)
Affirmed by Vaughn v. Public Emples. Ret. Sys. of Miss., 182 So. 3d 433, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 559 (Miss., Nov. 12, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/21/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED THE DECISION OF THE PUBLIC EMPLOYEES' RETIREMENT SYSTEM TO PAY THE ACTUARIAL EQUIVALENT OF GUARANTEED PAYMENTS TO THE RETIREE'S STATUTORY SUCCESSORS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a dispute over retirement benefits, the Mississippi Legislature intended for Miss. Code Ann. § 25-11-117.1(1) to govern payment of the lump-sum actuarial equivalent of any remaining future payments, while § 25-11-117.1(2) was to govern payments already sent to the beneficiary and any other benefit that was still payable at the death of the beneficiary; [2]-The retiree's family got the actuarial equivalent of the remaining guaranteed payments when both the retiree and her designated beneficiary (or beneficiaries) were dead; [3]-The limited exception was that any monthly check already written but not cashed by the deceased beneficiary (plus any cost-of-living adjustment for payments already made) were paid to that beneficiary's surviving family members.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Crook v. City of Madison


NO. 2013-KM-00081-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


168 So. 3d 1169; 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 536



September 30, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted Crook v. City of Madison, 154 So. 3d 33, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 5 (Miss., 2015)
Reversed by Crook v. City of Madison, 168 So. 3d 930, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 352 (Miss., July 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/12/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN HUEY EMFINGER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED CONVICTION OF TWO COUNTS OF VIOLATING A CITY ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF MADISON AND FINE OF $300 ON EACH COUNT. DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED - 03/25/2014. MOTION FOR REHEARING FILED: 04/08/2014 - DENIED.
Crook v. City of Madison, 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 170 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 25, 2014)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant had standing to assert the Madison, Mississippi, Rental Inspection and Property Licensing Act (RIPLA) was unconstitutional because his arrest and conviction for violating it involved a colorable interest in the case's subject matter and showed his unique adverse effect; [2]-RIPLA did not violate the Fourth Amendment because officials inspecting rental properties had to secure a warrant if entry were refused, and owners had advance notice; [3]-RIPLA did not violate Miss. Code Ann. § 21-17-5(2)(h) (Supp. 2013), barring rent regulation, because it did not directly or indirectly regulate rent; [4]-Defendant's arrest was improper because he should have first been noticed to appear in court; [5]-The evidence showed he rented property without a license because his agreements with two occupants of his property were rental in nature.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Baxter v. State


NO. 2012-KA-01032-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


177 So. 3d 423; 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 413



July 29, 2014, Decided

Affirmed by Baxter v. State, 177 So. 3d 394, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 389 (Miss., Aug. 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GEORGE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/15/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD W. MCKENZIE. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PAROLE, WITH THE SENTENCE TO RUN CONSECUTIVELY TO THE SENTENCES IN CAUSE NUMBERS 2009-10,073 AND 2010-10,057.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly admitted evidence obtained as a result of a deputy's pursuit because he acted reasonably in attempting to determine whether defendant was in a truck and obtained probable cause for an arrest once the truck sped away; [2]-The trial court correctly sentenced defendant to life without parole because the evidence was sufficient to find defendant guilty of capital murder under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(a) (Supp. 2013) (as a principal or an accessory) and parole was not an option for capital murder under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(1) (Rev. 2006) where the jury was allowed to find defendant guilty of capital murder whether he was the driver or whether his girlfriend was the driver of the truck that hit the sheriff and defendant confessed that he saw uniformed deputies at a blocked intersection and that he "nudged" one of them.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

281 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


NO. 2013-KA-00501-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


154 So. 3d 64; 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 338



June 17, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Williams v. State, 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 548 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 30, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/04/2013. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM E. CHAPMAN III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF EVASION CAUSING DEATH AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO FORTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS, WITHOUT THE POSSIBILITY OF PAROLE, PROBATION, OR SUSPENSION OR REDUCTION OF SENTENCE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant was properly convicted of vehicular evasion causing death, under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-9-72 (2006). HOLDINGS: [1]-No unconstitutional vagueness was shown either on the face of the statute or as applied to defendant's case; [2]-The evidence supported defendant's conviction because defendant's flight from the police was a direct and proximate cause of the victim's death in that defendant, while fleeing from the police, recklessly hit the victim's vehicle with his vehicle, after blindly running a red light at 60 miles per hour, and killed her. Even if it were assumed that the police pursuit was unreasonable, it could not be said to be a superseding cause because it was not an independent intervening agency, but instead was a natural and foreseeable response to defendant's flight; [3]-Defendant was not entitled to a lesser-included offense instruction.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Miller v. Provident Adver. & Mktg.


NO. 2012-CA-01198-COA CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2013-CA-00262-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


155 So. 3d 181; 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 339



June 17, 2014, Decided

Writ of certiorari denied, En banc Miller v. Provident Adver. & Mktg., 154 So. 3d 33, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 29 (Miss., 2015)
Writ of certiorari denied, En banc Miller v. Provident Adver. & Mktg., 2015 Miss. LEXIS 34 (Miss., Jan. 15, 2015)
Writ of certiorari denied, En banc Miller v. Provident Adver. & Mktg., 2015 Miss. LEXIS 32 (Miss., Jan. 15, 2015)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Cladakis v. Miller, 2015 U.S. LEXIS 4230 (U.S., June 22, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/11/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GERALD W. CHATHAM SR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: APPELLEES' MOTIONS TO DISMISS GRANTED.

COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/6/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: GERALD W. CHATHAM SR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR COSTS AND ATTORNEYS' FEES GRANTED IN FAVOR OF APPELLEE ANNA CLADAKIS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART. REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A trial court had personal jurisdiction over a former wife's alienation of affection claim under the Mississippi long-arm statute in Miss. Code Ann. § 13-3-57 (Rev. 2012) because the complaint stated a cause of action for a tort committed at least in part in Mississippi; [2]-There was an allegation of sexual activity between a paramour and the wife's husband within the state of Mississippi that contributed to the breakup of the marriage; [3]-However, the minimum contacts of the paramour could not have been attributed to her employers under principals of agency since there was no showing of how any sexual impropriety between the paramour and the husband was related to the scope of the paramour's employment; [4]-The fact that sexual activity occurred in Mississippi constituted purposeful availment for purposes of personal jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part, and reversed and rendered in part.

Manhattan Nursing & Rehab. Ctr., LLC v. Pace


NO. 2012-CA-00025-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


134 So. 3d 810; 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 169



March 25, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/14/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. TOMIE T. GREEN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: JURY AWARDED $1,200,000 IN NONECONOMIC DAMAGES TO APPELLEES, AND $13,300 IN ECONOMIC DAMAGES; TRIAL COURT REDUCED AWARD TO $513,300.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In this wrongful death case, the family's refusal of treatment was relevant to the issue of whether they failed to mitigate their damages; [2]-The jury should have been allowed to determine whether the decision to refuse certain treatments proximately caused the patient's death, since the jury was charged with determining the cause of the patient's death; [3]-The trial court erred in preventing cross-examination of a family member about documents showing the family's decision to withhold allegedly life-saving treatments from the patient; [4]-The hearsay exception under Miss. R. Evid. 803(4) was not applicable because the rule relates only to statements made to health-care providers by individuals seeking medical treatment, and the statements made by the family members were hearsay statements alleging what the physicians allegedly said about the patient's condition.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

285 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Crook v. City of Madison


NO. 2013-KM-00081-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 170



March 25, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Crook v. City of Madison, 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 554 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 30, 2014)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing denied by Crook v. City of Madison, 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 536 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 30, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/12/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN HUEY EMFINGER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED CONVICTION OF TWO COUNTS OF VIOLATING A CITY ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF MADISON AND FINE OF $300 ON EACH COUNT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Since the Rental Inspection and Property Licensing Act (RIPLA) of the City of City of Madison, Mississippi, incorporated a warrant-requirement provision in its inspection procedure, it was not unconstitutional; [2]-Section 7 of the RIPLA, detailed the instances in which access for an inspection could be warranted, but building officials had a duty, by virtue of the rental license, to secure a warrant authorizing entry in the event that the tenant or owner refused entry; [3]-In section 8 of the RIPLA, owners were afforded advance notice as to the date and time of any inspection; [3]-RIPLA did not violate the statute prohibiting municipalities from regulating rental rates, Miss. Code Ann. § 21-17-5(2)(h) (Supp. 2013), since it did not set a minimum or maximum rental rate, establish a formula to aid in establishing rental rates, or require the landlord to submit rental rates.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Cannon v. State


NO. 2012-KA-01551-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


141 So. 3d 442; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 853



December 10, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Cannon v. State, 2014 Miss. App. LEXIS 243 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 29, 2014)
Writ of certiorari dismissed Cannon v. State, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 329 (Miss., July 17, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: BOLIVAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/18/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ALBERT B. SMITH III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF COUNT I, SALE OF COCAINE WITHIN 1,500 FEET OF A PUBLIC PARK, COUNT II, SALE OF MARIJUANA WITHIN 1,500 FEET OF A PUBLIC PARK, AND COUNT III, CHILD ENDANGERMENT, AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO THIRTY YEARS FOR COUNT I AND AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO THREE YEARS FOR COUNT II, AND AS A NON-HABITUAL OFFENDER TO TEN YEARS FOR COUNT III, WITH ALL SENTENCES TO RUN CONCURRENTLY, ALL IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant was properly convicted of the sale of cocaine and marijuana within 1,500 feet of a public park and of child-endangerment. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Ross v. State


NO. 2011-CA-01770-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


122 So. 3d 136; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 626



September 24, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PONTOTOC COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/13/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES LAMAR ROBERTS JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.
Ross v. State, 802 So. 2d 171, 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 534 (Miss. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether revocation of a probationer's probation was appropriate. HOLDINGS: [1]-Pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-20 (2012), the probationer had to pay a fine immediately and/or the fine was a condition of probation because no installment plan was set up; [2]-The trial court did not err by revoking the post-release supervision, based solely on the probationer's failure to pay costs of court, a fine, and post-release supervision fees, because, while the probationer could not be held responsible for making payments while incarcerated, upon his release he became gainfully employed and, as he admitted, was making enough money to pay the costs and fines levied against him, and could pay, as well, a monthly sum toward costs of his supervision, as he was ordered to do.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Aydelott v. Quartaro


NO. 2011-CA-01880-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


124 So. 3d 97; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 327



June 4, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Aydelott v. Quartaro, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 695 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 22, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ITAWAMBA COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/07/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. TALMADGE D. LITTLEJOHN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: AWARDED GRANDPARENT VISITATION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Grandparents failed to show that they met the criterion of the establishment of a viable relationship with their granddaughters under Miss. Code Ann. § 93-16-3 (Supp. 2012); [2]-The chancellor erred in ignoring the grandparents' admissions and permitting contradictory testimony that they had contributed financially and had frequently visited the grandchildren because they never moved for withdrawal or amendment of their admissions, and thus, the lack of financial contribution or frequent visitation were deemed admitted under Miss. R. Civ. P. 36; [3]-Because the chancellor did not give the statute the necessary narrower reading, his explicit finding of a viable relationship and implicit finding of unreasonable denial of visitation failed to pass constitutional muster; [4]-The chancellor erred in weighing the grandparents' wishes into whether there was a viable relationship.


OUTCOME: Visitation award reversed.

 

301 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Hye v. State


NO. 2010-KA-01780-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


162 So. 3d 818; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 292



May 28, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Hye v. State, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 654 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 8, 2013)
Writ of certiorari granted Hye v. State, 131 So. 3d 577, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 19 (Miss., 2014)
Affirmed in part and vacated in part by, Remanded by Hye v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 69 (Miss., Feb. 5, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/05/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DALE HARKEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE WITHOUT PAROLE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The indictment charging defendant juvenile with capital murder was not defective, even though it referenced Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-79 (2006) and did not provide the essential elements of the underlying crime of robbery since it put defendant juvenile on notice that he was being charged with capital murder based on a robbery and defendant was aware that the charged underlying felony was robbery and not armed robbery; [2]-Defendant was not entitled to an accomplice instruction as the purported accomplice was an accessory-after-the-fact; [3]-The indictment was not defective because Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e) (2006), was cited in the heading, but not the body, as the indictment listed the proper provisions in the heading and tracked the statute in the body, and Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-20 did not specify where the charged section and subsection numbers had to appear.


OUTCOME: Defendant's capital murder conviction affirmed. Life sentence without parole vacated and case remanded for resentencing.

Hymes v. State


NO. 2011-CA-01688-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


121 So. 3d 938; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 272



May 21, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Hymes v. State, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 585 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 17, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WASHINGTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/31/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. ASHLEY HINES. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: ENTERED JUDGMENT IN FAVOR OF THE APPELLEE.
Hymes v. State, 703 So. 2d 258, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 638 (Miss., 1997)
Hymes v. McIlwain, 856 So. 2d 416, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 250 (Miss. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Appellant sued the State pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-44-7(1), seeking compensation for his alleged wrongful conviction and imprisonment. The trial court entered judgment for the State. Appellant sought review, claiming he was wrongfully convicted of possession of a firearm by a felon (Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5(1)) because the firearm he possessed was inoperable. The appellate court disagreed. He offered no evidence that the firearm could not be readily converted to expel a projectile, and § 97-37-5(1) did not require the State to prove that it was operable at the time of his arrest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

129 So. 3d 208; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 223

Writ of certiorari denied Fox v. State, 131 So. 3d 577, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 78 (Miss., 2014)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Fox v. Smith, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 5162 (N.D. Miss., Jan. 14, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/26/2012. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GERALD W. CHATHAM SR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DENIED MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION COLLATERAL RELIEF.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of leaving the scene of the accident and two counts of aggravated assault, appealed the lower court's denial of his motion for post-conviction collateral relief (PCCR). The appellate court held that the indictment charging appellant with leaving the scene of the accident was sufficient and not vague; as it included the phrase "wilfully, unlawfully, and feloniously," it was apparent that he was charged under the felony, not the misdemeanor, portion of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-3-401 (Supp. 2012).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

304 of 603 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of a Minor Child v. M.J.W.


NO. 2011-CA-01438-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


111 So. 3d 1243; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 150



April 2, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NEWTON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/04/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. H. DAVID CLARK II. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: APPELLANT'S PETITION TO SET ASIDE ADOPTION DISMISSED WITH PREJUDICE; APPELLANT'S PARENTAL RIGHTS TERMINATED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: While it was undisputed that a child's biological father did not receive formal notice of the adoption of his son, this did not void the adoption of the son as, even if the father had received notice, he did not meet the standard of demonstrating a full commitment to the responsibilities of parenthood under Miss. Code Ann. § 93-17-5(3), which would have allowed him, as an unwed father, to object to the adoption. There was no evidence that the father provided support for the child, that he tried to visit with the child, or that he was now willing and able to assume physical care for the child.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Cassidy v. State


NO. 2010-KA-01273-COA CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2011-CA-01815-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


110 So. 3d 335; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 123



March 5, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/25/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MELVIN V. PRIESTER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION OF COCAINE AND SENTENCED AS A SUBSEQUENT DRUG OFFENDER TO THIRTY-TWO YEARS, WITH TEN YEARS SUSPENDED AND FIVE YEARS OF POSTRELEASE SUPERVISION, ALL IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/04/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM A. GOWAN JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DENIED MOTION TO EXPUNGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion by refusing to permit defense counsel to cross-examine the State's key witness about her alleged prostitution and felony arrests under Miss. R. Evid. 609(a). Because the charges had not resulted in a conviction, they were properly excluded. The trial court should have allowed defense counsel to cross-examine the witness regarding any favorable treatment she could have received with regard to the alleged prostitution. However, the error was harmless because it did not contribute to the charge for which defendant was convicted.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Hampton v. State


NO. 2011-KA-01641-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


148 So. 3d 1038; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 73



February 19, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Hampton v. State, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 378 (Miss. Ct. App., June 25, 2013)
Writ of certiorari granted Hampton v. State, 119 So. 3d 328, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 457 (Miss., 2013)
Affirmed by Hampton v. State, 148 So. 3d 992, 2014 Miss. LEXIS 513 (Miss., Oct. 16, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/31/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WALTER BAILEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF ROBBERY BY USE OF A DEADLY WEAPON AND SENTENCED TO TWENTY YEARS AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PROBATION, PAROLE, EARNED TIME, OR GOOD-TIME CREDIT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In an armed robbery case, defendant's claim that his 19.5 year sentence was illegal under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-79 because it exceeded his life expectancy was not properly preserved for review as he did not object at sentencing and the circuit court did not commit plain error pursuant to Miss. R. App. P. 28(a)(3). Procedural bars aside, as a 63-year-old man, defendant had a life expectancy of 20.2 years. The circuit judge actually sentenced him to serve 19.5 years. As 19.5 was less than 20.2, defendant's claim lacked merit.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

307 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Hopkins v. City of Mendenhall


NO. 2011-CA-01633-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


116 So. 3d 166; 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 42



January 29, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Hopkins v. City of Mendenhall, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 379 (Miss. Ct. App., June 25, 2013)
Decision reached on appeal by Hopkins v. City of Mendenhall, 2015 Miss. App. LEXIS 507 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SIMPSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/30/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD W. MCKENZIE. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PETITION TO CLOSE STREET IN MENDENHALL GRANTED.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A judgment upholding the adoption of Mendenhall, Miss., Ord. 244 was reversed and the case was remanded with instructions to the City to provide reasons for the ordinance. The ordinance closed and vacated a portion of a street in the City. While the City had the authority under Miss. Code Ann. § 21-37-7 (2007) to close and vacate a street, it had to find the closing was for the public good under Miss. Code. Ann. §§ 21-13-1, 21-13-3 and 21-37-7 (2007). A street could not be closed just to benefit a private party. As no reason was given for the ordinance, the matter could not be reviewed.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. Case remanded with instructions.

KGC Props. v. Triangle Maint. Servs. LLC

OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Peterson v. State


NO. 2011-CP-01504-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


119 So. 3d 1068; 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 684



November 13, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Peterson v. State, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 187 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 23, 2013)
Writ of certiorari denied, En banc Peterson v. State, 119 So. 3d 328, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 410 (Miss., Aug. 8, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/13/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROGER T. CLARK. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR PAROLE OR CONDITIONAL RELEASE FROM PRISON DENIED.
Peterson v. State, 740 So. 2d 940, 1999 Miss. App. LEXIS 95 (Miss. Ct. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The denial of the inmate's petition for parole or conditional release from prison was proper under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-139(1)(a) (Rev. 2011) because the statutory requirements did not constitute a violation of his constitutional rights. Prisoners had no constitutionally recognized liberty interest in parole. Section 47-5-139 was not violative of an inmate's due process and equal protection rights by specifying criteria to consider in determining which inmates may or may not be considered for earned time allowance.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Higginbotham v. State


NO. 2011-CP-00972-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


114 So. 3d 9; 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 595



September 25, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Higginbotham v. State, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 317 (Miss., May 30, 2013)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Judgment entered by Higginbotham v. King, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 82147 (N.D. Miss., June 11, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WINSTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/16/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOSEPH H. LOPER JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The denial of a PCR request was affirmed. Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-21 was not unconstitutionally vague and did not apply to the inmate. The inmate confused parole with conditional release. Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3(1)(f) (2011) prohibited parole for an inmate sentenced to life under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101 for capital offenses. Since the inmate pled guilty to murder, carrying a life sentence, he was convicted of an other capital offense under Miss. Code Ann. § 1-3-4 (2005). The inmate was eligible to petition for conditional release at age 65 under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-139(1)(a) (2011).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Wilson v. State


NO. 2011-CP-00315-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


95 So. 3d 1282; 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 538



August 28, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/20/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SAMAC S. RICHARDSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon (PFCF) (Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5) and carrying a concealed weapon (CCW) (Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-1), appealed the denial of his postconviction relief (CPR) petition. The PCR court properly rejected his claim that his conviction of both charges violated the double jeopardy ban. As a conviction of PFCF required proof of a prior felony, while a conviction of CCW required proof the weapon was concealed, each offense had an element not present in the other; therefore, there was no double jeopardy violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A teacher sued appellee, the conservator of a school district, challenging his termination for neglect of duty. The trial court affirmed; the teacher appealed. The appellate court held that the teacher's inability to make a final statement pursuant to Miss. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Chapell v. State


NO. 2011-CA-00336-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


107 So. 3d 1003; 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 366



June 19, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Chapell v. State, 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 666 (Miss. Ct. App., Nov. 6, 2012)
Writ of certiorari denied Chapell v. State, 107 So. 3d 998, 2013 Miss. LEXIS 104 (Miss., 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Chapell v. Winkel, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 118732 (N.D. Miss., July 21, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/17/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES MCCLURE III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged a judgment dismissing his motion for post-conviction relief. Defendant's sentence did not violate the Eighth Amendment. The circuit court did not err by failing to conduct a proportionality review. A threshold comparison of the crimes and sentences did not lead to an inference of gross disproportionality. Defendants' crimes, sexual battery of a minor and fondling, compared to his twenty-five year sentence was not excessive. The sentence imposed was only five years more than the minimum for each sexual battery charge and ordered the sentences to run concurrently.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

314 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Townes v. State


NO. 2011-CP-00710-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


88 So. 3d 812; 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 278



May 15, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/29/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT P. CHAMBERLIN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: An inmate's PCR motion against the State was properly denied because the inmate's claim that he had new evidence of a material fact under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(1)(e) (Supp. 2011)-namely, that he was acting in self-defense-consisted only of his own version of the incident. This defense was available to the inmate at the time of his guilty plea. Further, newly discovered evidence was relevant only where a defendant went to trial and was convicted. Because the inmate testified at his plea that he was satisfied with his counsel's services, his claim of ineffective assistance lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hills v. State


NO. 2011-CP-00376-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


101 So. 3d 691; 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 281



May 15, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Hills v. State, 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 559 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 11, 2012)
Writ of certiorari denied Hills v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 587 (Miss., Nov. 29, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/22/2011. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DAVID H. STRONG JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DISMISSED MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed a judgment that dismissed his motion for postconviction relief (PCR). The appellate court found, inter alia, that while the indictment did not specifically use the phrase "date of judgment," it was sufficient to notify him of the prior convictions that were used to enhance his sentence. Therefore, his sentence was not illegal. In addition, defendant did not show how the outcome of the proceedings would have been different had his attorney objected to the indictment. Therefore, defendant was not entitled to PCR.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Payton v. State


NO. 2010-CP-01488-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


89 So. 3d 73; 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 747



December 6, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Payton v. State, 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 292 (Miss. Ct. App., May 22, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ATTALA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/10/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOSEPH H. LOPER JR.. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION COLLATERAL RELIEF DISMISSED.
Payton v. State, 661 So. 2d 733, 1995 Miss. LEXIS 468 (Miss., 1995)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The dismissal of appellant's postconviction relief (PCR) motion was improper. He filed in the wrong court and the supreme court did not have jurisdiction. Apparently, he was correct to proceed with his PCR motion before the circuit court. As a result, the appellate court was required to reverse the circuit court's judgment where it dismissed the PCR motion based on its lack of jurisdiction. On remand, the circuit court could consider the PCR motion even though the supreme court denied the application.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.
