Mangum v. Miss. Parole Bd.


NO. 2010-CP-00822-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


76 So. 3d 762; 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 727



November 29, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/02/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.
Mangum v. State, 64 So. 3d 503, 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 611 (Miss. Ct. App., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Prisoner properly stated a claim for racial-discrimination against the Mississippi Parole Board because he provided specific examples of unequal treatment. Although the circuit court had no jurisdiction to review whether the Board properly denied parole, it did have jurisdiction to determine the prisoner's racial-discrimination claim if service of process had been accomplished. To the extent that the prisoner's claim was based on an allegation of improper motive, race, he asserted a cognizable constitutional claim under the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded.

Durham v. State


NO. 2010-KA-00728-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


74 So. 3d 908; 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 690



November 8, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/03/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT B. HELFRICH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF COUNTS I-IV, FELONY BAD CHECK, AND SENTENCED TO THREE YEARS ON EACH COUNT, WITH THE SENTENCES TO RUN CONSECUTIVELY, IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS, WITH THREE YEARS SUSPENDED AND THREE YEARS OF POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION OF THE SENTENCE IN COUNT IV.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of writing bad checks with fraudulent intent, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-19-55(1)(a). A jury instruction that tracked the language Miss. Code Ann. § 97-19-57(1) created a mandatory presumption, and the circuit court failed to shift the burden of proof away from defendant by instructing the jury about the "prima facie" inference of intent to defraud. No explanation of the term "prima facie" was provided to the jury, nor was there any instruction that regardless of the presumption, the burden of proof remained on the State to prove intent to defraud beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded for a new trial.

320 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Yates


NO. 2009-CA-02032-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


68 So. 3d 758; 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 488



August 16, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/26/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DAN H. FAIRLY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: REQUEST FOR GRANDPARENT'S VISITATION DENIED.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: After a paternal grandmother filed a petition for grandparent visitation pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 93-16-3(1), the chancery court denied visitation. On appeal, the court found that, because the chancery court failed to grant grandparent visitation despite finding that the factors which were to be considered favored visitation and that visitation was in the minor child's best interest, remand for an award of limited visitation consistent with the chancery court's analysis and the child's best interest was appropriate.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, and case remanded.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/19/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM E. CHAPMAN III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF DRIVING UNDER THE INFLUENCE, FIRST OFFENSE, AND SENTENCED TO FORTY-EIGHT HOURS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE SHERIFF OF MADISON COUNTY, WITH THE SENTENCE SUSPENDED FOR TWO YEARS UNLESS SOONER INVOKED ON CERTAIN SPECIFIED CONDITIONS, AND TO PAY A FINE OF $700.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Madison County Circuit Court, Mississippi, for driving under the influence, first offense. Thus, defendant's right to confrontation was not violated by the admission of the certificates as they were non-testimonial in nature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Devereaux v. State


NO. 2010-KA-00710-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


83 So. 3d 387; 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 301



May 31, 2011, Decided


NOTICE: NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Devereaux v. State, 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 560 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 20, 2011)
Writ of certiorari granted, En banc Devereaux v. State, 78 So. 3d 906, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 28 (Miss., 2012)
Writ of certiorari dismissed Devereaux v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 157 (Miss., Mar. 22, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/21/2010. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF BURGLARY OF A BUILDING OTHER THAN A DWELLING AND SENTENCED TO SEVEN YEARS WITHOUT PAROLE OR PROBATION; AND CONVICTED OF GRAND LARCENY AND SENTENCED TO TEN YEARS, TO RUN CONSECUTIVELY TO THE BURGLARY SENTENCE WITHOUT PAROLE OR PROBATION, ALL IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Tate County Circuit Court, Mississippi, of burglary of a building other than a dwelling and grand larceny. The trial court found that he was a habitual offender and sentenced him to an effective term of 17 years with no possibility of parole, probation, or a reduction of his sentence. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: During his interrogation, defendant asked for a public defender who had previously represented him. Counsel was located and joined defendant. The court found that under no circumstances should defendant have been prompted to sign a form waiving his Miranda right to counsel when he had already requested counsel and the requested lawyer was present in the room with him. Further, defendant had every reason to believe that counsel was acting as his attorney during the interrogation. Defendant's fragile mental condition also required the presence of a lawyer. Defendant did not voluntarily, knowingly, or intelligently waive his right to counsel. Thus, defendant's constitutional rights were violated during the interrogation, and the trial court committed reversible error by admitting a videotape of the interrogation into evidence. The court also found reversible error in the trial court's failure to address defendant's receipt of constitutionally defective assistance of counsel during his interrogation. As admission of the videotape into evidence forced defendant to give up his right to remain silent and testify in his own defense, his Fifth Amendment rights were again violated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial.

Crutcher v. State


NO. 2009-KA-01819-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


68 So. 3d 724; 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 205



April 12, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Crutcher v. State, 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 414 (Miss. Ct. App., June 21, 2011)
Writ of certiorari denied Crutcher v. State, 69 So. 3d 767, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 415 (Miss., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied, Motion dismissed by, As moot Crutcher v. Mississippi, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 155375 (N.D. Miss., Oct. 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/05/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT P. CHAMBERLIN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF SALE OF A CONTROLLED SUBSTANCE AND SENTENCED TO SIXTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AS A HABITUAL AND SUBSEQUENT OFFENDER WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PAROLE OR PROBATION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of selling cocaine. The DeSoto County Circuit Court, Mississippi, sentenced him to 60 years in confinement as a habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 and as a subsequent offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-147. Defendant sought review, challenging the denial of his motion for a mistrial, the admission of a videotape into evidence, the chain of custody of the cocaine, and his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought a mistrial, claiming that the State, when conducting voir dire, improperly commented on his right to remain silent and not to testify. The court found no abuse of discretion in the denial of his motion as the prosecutor simply remarked that the defense was not required to put on any witnesses and did not speak to defendant's failure to testify. Defendant argued that the State failed to lay a sufficient evidentiary foundation to enter a videotape of the drug sale into evidence under Miss. R. Evid. 901(b)(1). The court concluded that the videotape was properly authenticated by two police officers who testified that the videotape accurately depicted the transaction as it occurred. Defendant presented no evidence or reasonable inference to support his claim that there was a break in the custody of the cocaine. Thus, he failed to overcome the presumption of regularity and the cocaine was properly admitted into evidence. The court concluded defendant's sentence complied with §§ 99-19-81 and 41-29-147. Given the gravity of the instant offense and the nature of his prior offenses, his sentence did not give rise to an inference of gross disproportionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

City of Jackson v. Rebuild Am., Inc.


NO. 2008-CA-02121-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


77 So. 3d 1105; 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 195



April 5, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by City of Jackson v. Rebuild Am., Inc., 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 558 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 20, 2011)
Writ of certiorari denied, En banc City of Jackson v. Rebuild Am., Inc., 78 So. 3d 906, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 27 (Miss., Jan. 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/17/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM H. SINGLETARY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: SUMMARY JUDGMENT GRANTED IN FAVOR OF REBUILD AMERICA, INC.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Certain real property was sold by tax sale to a bank. The bank sold the property to appellee purchaser. The purchaser filed an action to quiet title against appellant city. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The city claimed that the property had reverted to it by operation of law and that the tax sale was void. The Chancery Court of Hinds County, Mississippi, entered summary judgment for the purchaser. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city conveyed the property to a community development corporation (CDC) by quitclaim deed that contained a reverter clause as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 21-17-1(3)(a) (Rev. 2001 & Supp. 2003). The CDC failed to pay property taxes. The city claimed that the CDC did not receive proper notice of the expiration of the right of redemption under Miss. Code Ann. § 27-43-1 (Rev. 2006). Thus, the tax sale was void. The court found that the city had standing to assert such a claim. However, the city's argument that its reversionary interest was sufficient to require notice of the expiration of the right of redemption under § 27-43-1 was dispositive of the appeal. The court construed § 27-43-1's reference to "record owner" to include a holder of a reversionary interest. As the reverter language was on the face of the quitclaim deed to the CDC, the city's reversionary interest in the property was reasonably ascertainable, and it was entitled to receive statutory notice of the expiration of the redemption period from the chancery court clerk.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment for the purchaser and rendered summary judgment for the city.

5K Farms, Inc. v. Miss. State Tax Comm'n


NO. 2009-CA-01787-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


94 So. 3d 291; 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 141



March 15, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc 5K Farms, Inc. v. Miss. Dep't of Revenue, 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 466 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 9, 2011)
Writ of certiorari granted 5K Farms, Inc. v. Miss. Dep't of Revenue, 73 So. 3d 1168, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 541 (Miss., 2011)
Affirmed by 5K Farms, Inc. v. Miss. Dep't of Revenue, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 233 (Miss., May 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/21/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM H. SINGLETARY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DISMISSED FOR LACK OF SUBJECT-MATTER JURISDICTION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision from appellee Mississippi State Tax Commission, which assessed a fee against it as a commercial solid waste disposal site. The Hinds County Chancery Court, Mississippi, ruled that the taxpayer could not proceed with its appeal as an indigent party and was required to post the proper bond. The chancery court dismissed the case for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: After filing its appeal with the chancery court, the taxpayer filed a motion for supersedeas that requested the chancery court enter an order allowing it to proceed without posting a bond as required and to prevent any collection proceedings against it during the pendency of the case. The taxpayer attached a pauper's affidavit that asserted it did not have the money to pay the required bond or assessment. The court found that the language of Miss. Code Ann. § 27-7-7 (Rev. 2005) was clear. To appeal to the chancery court, the taxpayer was required to post a bond or pay the amount of the tax under protest. By doing neither, the chancery court did not err in dismissing the case. The taxpayer was not entitled to proceed in forma pauperis on an appeal from the Commission to the chancery court. The taxpayer argued that § 27-7-7 violated its due process rights. However, that matter was not before the chancery court nor did it notify the Attorney General of its constitutional challenge as required by Miss. R. Civ. P. 24(d) and Miss. R. App. P. 44(a), which resulted in a procedural bar to the court's review of that issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Mangum v. State


NO. 2009-CP-01167-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


64 So. 3d 503; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 611



November 9, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Mangum v. State, 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 201 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 5, 2011)
Writ of certiorari denied Mangum v. State, 63 So. 3d 1229, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 327 (Miss., 2011)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Mangum v. Miss. Parole Bd., 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 727 (Miss. Ct. App., Nov. 29, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/02/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.
Mangum v. State, 553 So. 2d 24, 1989 Miss. LEXIS 699 (Miss., 1989)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a fifth request for postconviction relief. The Circuit Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi) denied the motion. The inmate appealed. The inmate had pled guilty to murder and been sentenced to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion for postconviction relief, because his indictment failed to state the essential elements of the crime of murder. While the issue was not raised within the three-year limitations period in Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) or fall within any of the recognized exceptions, the issue was reviewable because it infringed upon the inmate's right to due process, which right was not waivable and was excepted from the procedural bars of the Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act. As for the merits of the claim, the appellate court concluded that the indictment was legally sufficient. While defendant claimed that the indictment should have included the phrase "not in necessary self-defense," the indictment's inclusion of the word "unlawfully" rendered the indictment legally sufficient.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the inmate's motion was affirmed.

Keys v. State


NO. 2009-CA-01050-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


67 So. 3d 783; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 565



October 19, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Keys v. State, 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 104 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 1, 2011)
Writ of certiorari granted Keys v. State, 62 So. 3d 974, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 259 (Miss., 2011)
Reversed by Keys v. State, 67 So. 3d 758, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 389 (Miss., Aug. 11, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/27/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT B. HELFRICH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment of the Forrest County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion to mandate parole eligibility on his life sentence pursuant to the Mississippi Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals held that the trial court lacked the jurisdiction necessary to consider the inmate's motion under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-803(2) (Rev. 2004). The inmate did not exhaust his administrative remedies. The trial court erroneously treated the inmate's motion as if it were a motion for post-conviction relief. However, the inmate's request did not complain about the validity of any of his convictions, of the sentences received, or that he was unlawfully incarcerated, which were some of the grounds for relief permitted under a motion for post-conviction relief pursuant to the Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(1)(a) - (i) (Supp. 2008). The inmate's motion simply argued that the Mississippi Department of Corrections (MDOC) had incorrectly classified him as "parole ineligible." A motion for post-conviction relief was not the correct procedural vehicle for such an argument. The MDOC had determined that the inmate was ineligible for parole consideration by the parole board. The record was completely bare as to any proof that the inmate ever exhausted his administrative remedies or even voiced his grievance through the MDOC's administrative-review procedure.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals reversed the judgment and dismissed the inmate's appeal for lack of jurisdiction.

 

337 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Decker v. State


NO. 2008-KA-01621-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


66 So. 3d 659; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 459



August 31, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Decker v. State, 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 685 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 14, 2010)
Writ of certiorari granted Decker v. State, 56 So. 3d 574, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 147 (Miss., 2011)
Reversed by Decker v. State, 66 So. 3d 654, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 379 (Miss., Aug. 4, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CLAY COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/01/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF FELONY EXPLOITATION OF A VULNERABLE ADULT AND SENTENCED TO FOUR YEARS IN THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS, WITH FOUR YEARS SUSPENDED, AND TO PAY $ 4,120 IN RESTITUTION AND A $ 250 FINE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of exploitation of a vulnerable adult by the Circuit Court of Clay County, Mississippi. The trial court gave her a 4-year suspended sentence, ordered her to pay a fine and court costs, and to pay restitution. Defendant filed a motion for a directed verdict, or, in the alternative, a motion for a new trial, which was denied. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused in the indictment of using $ 4,120 of her mother's money without her mother's consent at the time her mother was a vulnerable adult. However, the jury instruction stated that she could be found guilty if she exploited her mother by using her resources with or without her mother's consent. The court found that defendant was correct that the jury instruction failed to follow the language of the indictment, but it did follow the definition of exploitation set out in Miss. Code Ann. § 43-47-5(i) (2009). The testimony implied that defendant used the money for her son's benefit with her mother's consent. However, the statute made it clear that any improper use of a vulnerable adult's resources for another's advantage was exploitation. Consent was a non-issue as the State did not have to prove consent. Defendant argued that the § 43-47-5(i) was unconstitutional vague as there was no explanation of the terms "illegal" or "improper," which made it impossible to determine if a financial transaction was improper. The court found that under the language of the statute, her actions constituted exploitation. Thus, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

338 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Rochell v. State


NO. 2008-CP-01730-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


36 So. 3d 479; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 291



June 8, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/18/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WINSTON L. KIDD. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DISMISSED WITH PREJUDICE.
Rochell v. State, 913 So. 2d 993, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 191 (Miss. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed suit against appellee State, seeking an interpretation of Miss. Code Ann. §§ 47-7-3 and 47-7-5 (Supp. 2009) and claiming that they were unconstitutional. He moved for a preliminary injunction, alleging that the Mississippi State Parole Board violated his Fourteenth Amendment rights by arbitrarily denying him parole. He challenged a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed his complaint.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals held that the inmate's concerns failed to state a constitutional claim sufficient for the trial court to assert jurisdiction. Because the trial court lacked jurisdiction to consider the inmate's claims, it did not err by dismissing his complaint. The Parole Board was in compliance with Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-5, which provided that the Parole Board had to be composed of five members. The trial court did not err by denying the inmate's motion for a preliminary injunction. Nothing in the record supported the inmate's claim that the Parole Board arbitrarily denied him parole in violation of any Fourteenth Amendment right. The Parole Board denied the inmate's parole based upon the serious nature of the offense, the number of offenses committed, the inmate's police record, community opposition, and insufficient time served. The reasons stated by the Parole Board for denying the inmate's parole were areas that the Parole Board had authority to consider under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-17 (Rev. 2004). Therefore, those categories could not be viewed as arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the judgment.

Summerall v. State


NO. 2009-KA-00110-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


41 So. 3d 729; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 280



June 8, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at Summerall v. State, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 829 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/13/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT B. HELFRICH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION OF A WEAPON BY A CONVICTED FELON AND SENTENCED TO TEN YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of possession of a dirk knife by a convicted felon in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5 (Supp. 2009). The Forrest County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denied defendant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV), or in the alternative, a new trial. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 97-37-5 was unconstitutionally vague as it provided insufficient notice of the contemplated conduct it prohibited. The court disagreed, finding that it specifically prohibited felons from possessing dirk knives. Thus, defendant failed to overcome the statute's presumption of validity. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion JNOV because the State offered insufficient evidence to prove that the knife he was in possession of was a dirk knife. The court observed that the legislature had never defined the term "dirk knife." In examining the traditional and modern views of the definition of a dirk knife from other jurisdictions, the court concluded that to qualify as a dirk knife for purposes of § 97-37-5, a weapon had to have a blade with at least one sharpened edge that tapered to a point and had to be designed for use primarily as a stabbing weapon. The court concluded that the evidence failed to show that the knife in defendant's possession at the time of his arrest was a dirk knife.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and rendered a judgment of acquittal.

Ryals v. State


NO. 2009-CP-00839-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


51 So. 3d 974; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 262



June 1, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Ryals v. State, 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 556 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 12, 2010)
Writ of certiorari denied Ryals v. State, 50 So. 3d 1003, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 47 (Miss., 2011)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Ryals v. Abrams, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 98709 (S.D. Miss., Aug. 16, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/30/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LISA P. DODSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DISMISSED MOTION TO VACATE AND SET ASIDE CONVICTION AND SENTENCE.
Ryals v. State, 881 So. 2d 933, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 903 (Miss. Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Forrest County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which summarily dismissed his motion to vacate and set aside his conviction of capital murder and sentence as a successive writ that was time-barred.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to a charge of killing his wife during the commission of a robbery, and he was sentenced to life in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections without the possibility of parole. He filed a pro se motion to vacate and set aside his conviction of capital murder and sentence. The trial court summarily dismissed his motion as a successive writ and as time-barred. Defendant appealed, but the appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Defendant's motion for post-conviction relief presently was barred as a successive writ because his previous motion for post-conviction relief raised the same arguments. In addition, those arguments did not fall within the purview of the exceptions to the successive-writ bar, Miss. Code Ann. § 88-39-23(6) (2009). While his petition raised three new issues, they could have been raised in his first motion for post-conviction relief; thus, he was procedurally barred from raising them in a second petition.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

DISPOSITION: VACATED & REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an insanity acquittee, challenged a judgment of the Walthall County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied a state hospital's request for the conditional release of the insanity acquittee and ordered that he remain at the state hospital.

During the pendency of the appeal, the legislature established a procedure for considering the release of insanity acquittees, which was to be codified as Miss. Code Ann. § 99-13-7(2). Because the circuit court made no findings regarding his mental state or his dangerousness to the community, as required by the new legislation, the court vacated the judgment and remanded the case.

Walker v. State


NO. 2008-CP-01987-COA CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2008-CP-01988-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


35 So. 3d 555; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 167



March 30, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/06/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R.I. PRICHARD III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.
Walker v. State, 861 So. 2d 354, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 1132 (Miss. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged judgments of the Circuit Court of Marion County (Mississippi), which dismissed his motion for post-conviction collateral relief, his petition for an order to show cause, and his petition to clarify sentence.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued the circuit court erred in addressing his petitions to show cause and clarify his sentence under the Mississippi Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act. The court of appeals held that the inmate's petitions to clarify and show cause had to be handled initially under administrative-review procedures, rather than in the courts, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-803 (Rev. 2004). Since there was no indication in the record that the inmate exhausted his administrative remedies on those claims, the court of appeals are without jurisdiction to consider them. The inmate argued that his parole was unlawfully revoked. The inmate's due-process rights were not violated when his parole was revoked. Upon receiving a certified copy of the order of the court of appeals, the parole board had authority pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. 47-7-27 to immediately revoke the inmate's parole on his earlier conviction. A preliminary revocation hearing and a parole-revocation hearing were held. The parole board then sent the inmate a letter, which provided notice of its decision to revoke his parole and afforded an opportunity to present evidence on his behalf.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the judgments dismissing the inmate's motions for post-conviction relief.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/23/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Approximately 13 years after his conviction for the sale of crack cocaine, defendant filed a petition to show cause complaining that he had been denied effective assistance of counsel. The Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) treated the petition as one for post-conviction relief and denied the petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly construed his petition as one for post-conviction relief or a claim based upon a deprivation of his civil rights. Code Ann. § 99-39-7 (Supp. 2009) to receive leave from the Mississippi Supreme Court before he filed his petition for post-conviction relief. Having failed to do so, the petition was procedurally barred. Further, defendant improperly filed his petition in the wrong circuit and the petition was untimely pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (2007).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismiss the petition.

Graham v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI

Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Graham v. State, 2011 Miss. App. LEXIS 33 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/20/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILLY JOE LANDRUM. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In Jones County Circuit Court (Mississippi), appellant was indicted for possession of 11.59 grams of cocaine with the intent to distribute pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-142 (2005). Appellant pled guilty and was sentenced. Appellant violated the terms of his house arrest and was serving the rest of his sentence in custody. The circuit court denied appellant's timely filed motion for postconviction relief and appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The assignments of error included: the circuit court and defense counsel failed to advise him of his right to appeal his sentence; the sentence imposed constituted an unconstitutional, illegal sentence; he was denied effective assistance of counsel; and his guilty plea was not voluntarily and intelligently entered. Appellant's arguments failed. The circuit court erred in determining it lacked jurisdiction to review appellant's motion for postconviction relief. Even if appellant's counsel failed to advise him of his right to appeal his sentence, appellant did not allege that he would have appealed his illegally lenient sentence. Any such claim would have been viewed with skepticism, as it was not in appellant's interest to appeal the sentence until four months later when his intensive supervision program status was revoked. The circuit judge carefully questioned appellant about his ability to understand the charges against him, the repercussions of his guilty plea, and his willingness to enter into the plea arrangement. The circuit court found appellant's decision was freely, voluntarily, and intelligently made and accepted his plea.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court denying the motion for postconviction relief was affirmed. All costs of the appeal were assessed to the county.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARSHALL COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/27/2009. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW K. HOWORTH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.
Glass v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 1045 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 14, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pro se appellant inmate appealed the decision by the Marshall County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denying his second petition for post-conviction relief (PCR). He had pled guilty to violating Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(1)(a) (Rev. 2001). He asserted that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, his life sentence was excessive and unconstitutional, and other procedural errors, not raised before the trial court, merited reversal.


OVERVIEW: The only such exception that the inmate alleged allowed him to file a successive writ was the existence of an intervening decision. With regard solely to his proposed unconstitutional sentence, he argued that the Apprendi decision and the Blakely decision satisfied the intervening-decision exception. His argument was essentially that his sentence of life was unconstitutional because the trial court and not a jury decided his punishment. However, neither decision provided any support for his claim. Since the trial court imposed a sentence within the statutory limitations provided by the Mississippi Legislature, the inmate's sentence was appropriate, and there was no error. In addition to the procedural bar against a successive writ, the inmate's current petition, had it been his first plea for review, would nonetheless still be barred by the three-year statute of limitations in Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (Supp. 2009). He had pled guilty on March 1, 2001. His current petition for PCR was filed on October 1, 2008, well past the time limit granted to file for relief under the Mississippi Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Mayers v. State


NO. 2008-KA-01722-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


42 So. 3d 33; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 88



February 23, 2010, Decided

Writ of certiorari denied Mayers v. State, 42 So. 3d 24, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 437 (Miss., Aug. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/11/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SAMAC S. RICHARDSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF COUNT I, AGGRAVATED ASSAULT UPON A LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICER, AND SENTENCED TO THIRTY YEARS; COUNT II, AGGRAVATED ASSAULT UPON A LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICER, AND SENTENCED TO THIRTY YEARS; COUNT III, POSSESSION OF A STOLEN FIREARM, AND SENTENCED TO FIVE YEARS; COUNT IV, POSSESSION OF A FIREARM BY A CONVICTED FELON, AND SENTENCED TO THREE YEARS, AND SENTENCED TO TEN ADDITIONAL YEARS EACH FOR COUNTS I AND II, WITH THE SENTENCES TO RUN CONSECUTIVELY IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PAROLE OR PROBATION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Rankin County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of aggravated assault on law enforcement officers (Counts I and II), possession of a stolen firearm (Count III), and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon (Count IV). He was sentenced to 30 years for Counts I and II, 5 years for Count III, and 3 years for Count IV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentence and the appellate court reversed in part. Defendant was erroneously sentenced under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-37(2) (Supp. 2009), which was not in effect at the time his crime was committed. He should have been sentenced pursuant to section 97-37-37(1) (Supp. 2009), which became effective on July 1, 2004. Section 97-37-37(1) required a sentence enhancement of five years for each count of aggravated assault because defendant used a firearm during the commission of the felonies. The sentence enhancement under Counts I and II was vacated, and the case was remanded. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed. The heading of defendant's indictment stated that he was being charged with aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer and the counts stated the statute under which he was charged; thus, it was clear from the indictment that defendant injured the two police officers with a deadly weapon. His conviction under Count III was proper because an informant testified that he gave defendant a pistol in exchange for crack cocaine and that defendant knew that the pistol was stolen.


OUTCOME: The sentence enhancement under Counts I and II was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing pursuant to the law in effect at the time of defendant's crime. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

Field v. State


NO. 2008-KA-00793-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


28 So. 3d 697; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 101



February 23, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NEWTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/16/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. VERNON R. COTTEN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION OF COCAINE AND SENTENCED TO EIGHT YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of possession of marijuana; however, a mistrial was declared on a possession of cocaine charge as the jury was unable to reach a verdict. Subsequently, appellant was convicted by a jury in the Newton County Circuit Court (Mississippi) on a count of felony possession of cocaine and sentenced to eight years. It was from the second conviction that appellant raised four issues on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that: the circuit court erred in sentencing her to the maximum allowable sentence; the circuit court erred in refusing to give a jury instruction which allegedly articulated appellant's theory of the case; the circuit court erred in admitting evidence of other crimes; and the search of the truck appellant was driving was unreasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV. The arguments failed. Although appellant claimed she was a first-time offender, she was previously charged three times for driving under the influence and she was addicted to marijuana and alcohol. As the marijuana and the cocaine were in the same container within appellant's purse, the discovery of the marijuana led to the deputy's discovery of the cocaine at issue in the second trial. Further, appellant's admission that the marijuana was hers demonstrated that it was more likely that the cocaine was also hers. The checkpoint was set up in daylight, on a straight thoroughfare, and there was a definitive plan established by the officers for checking vehicles. Any minor deviation from the departmental policy was reasonable under the circumstances and did not violate appellant's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Henry v. State


NO. 2008-KA-01648-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


40 So. 3d 621; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 47



February 9, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Henry v. State, 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 400 (Miss. Ct. App., July 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/28/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF FELONY CHILD ABUSE AND SENTENCED TO TWENTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITH FIVE YEARS OF POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of felony child abuse in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-39(2)(a) (Rev. 2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for felony child abuse, but the appellate court affirmed. There was no question that defendant's attorney was engaged in the practice of law during his representation of defendant and the attorney's recent status change to inactive was harmless as it related to the jury verdict. Defendant failed to show prejudice because the attorney had been an inactive member for less than one month, which was clearly an insufficient period of time to claim that the attorney's continuing education was lacking. Additionally, defendant did not prove that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant failed to prove that the outcome of his trial was prejudiced by comments made by counsel, especially in light of the overwhelming weight of evidence against defendant, including defendant's own statement that he spanked and bit the child, coupled with eyewitness and medical testimony regarding the severity of the child's injuries. Medical testimony at trial further unequivocally proved that the victim's severe bruising was a temporary disfigurement of a bodily organ.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and costs of the appeal were assessed to defendant.

Jones v. Laurel Family Clinic, P.A.


NO. 2008-CA-01490-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


37 So. 3d 665; 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 14



January 5, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Jones v. Laurel Family Clinic, P.A., 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 333 (Miss. Ct. App., June 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/11/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILLY JOE LANDRUM. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: COMPLAINT DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a case brought under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (MTCA), appellant, the natural mother and adult next friend of a minor, sought judicial review of the decision by the Jones County Circuit Court (Mississippi) dismissing her medical negligence claim against defendant hospital without prejudice because she had not given the hospital 90 days' notice of the claim before filing the complaint. The mother alleged two claims on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the MTCA violated (1) the Equal Protection Clause of the Seventh and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution, and (2) the anti-trust, unfair competition, and price fixing provisions of the Sherman Anti-trust Act. Neither of the mother's arguments were presented to the circuit court. Therefore, the appellate court could not address them on appeal. Although, in her motion to amend the complaint, the mother stated that she wished to raise the constitutionality of the MTCA, there was no valid complaint to amend. She also had not provided the required notice under Miss. R. Civ. P. 24(d) to the Mississippi Attorney General that she was going to challenge the constitutionality of the MTCA. It was clear that she resorted to those novel claims on appeal because there was no error on the part of the circuit court. While the mother had given the hospital notice as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(1), she filed suit after only 85 days later, and the 90-day requirement in § 11-46-11(1) was a hard-edged, mandatory rule which the courts strictly enforced.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Williams v. State


NO. 2008-KP-00227-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


24 So. 3d 360; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 940



December 15, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/03/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SAMAC S. RICHARDSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF FELONY SHOPLIFTING AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO TEN YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PAROLE OR PROBATION AND TO PAY A FINE OF $ 10,000.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of felony shoplifting, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-23-93 (Supp. 2003). She was convicted and sentenced as a habitual offender by the Madison County Circuit Court (Mississippi). Appearing pro se, she appealed her 10-year sentence without eligibility for parole or probation as being unconstitutional and illegal.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court's denial of defendant's amended motion for a new trial on August 2, 2007, determined the starting date for the purposes of determining whether the appeal was untimely filed. While the appeal was untimely, the appellate court would suspend the rules and review her out-of-time appeal on the merits. Defendant unsuccessfully argued that she should not have been charged as a habitual offender as the sentences for her two previous convictions were served concurrently. Her two prior felonies were separate incidents, which occurred at different times, and each carried a sentence of at least one year. The fact that she was only incarcerated for one year while serving her concurrent sentences did not afford her relief from habitual offender status under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (Rev. 2000). Defendant argued unsuccessfully that her sentence was unconstitutional as it exceeded the maximum sentence allowed by law. As she was a habitual offender, the circuit court was required under § 99-19-81 to impose the maximum sentence for grand larceny, which was ten years and a fine of $ 10,000. Miss. Code Ann. § 97-17-41 (Supp. 2003).


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

Brown v. State


NO. 2008-KA-00944-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


37 So. 3d 1205; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 945



December 15, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Brown v. State, 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 161 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 30, 2010)
Writ of certiorari denied Brown v. State, 39 So. 3d 5, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 329 (Miss., 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Brown v. Mississippi, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 8510 (U.S., Nov. 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PONTOTOC COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/10/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION COCAINE, A SCHEDULE II CONTROLLED SUBSTANCE, AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PAROLE OR PROBATION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a Pontotoc County Circuit Court (Mississippi) jury of possession of cocaine, in an amount greater than.10 gram but less than 2 grams, and sentenced as a habitual offender to life in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections without eligibility for parole or probation. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant neither alleged jurisdictional defect in the indictment, nor did she identify any actual prejudice she suffered as a result of any non-jurisdictional defect, so her claim could not be raised for the first time in her appeal. Although the State subjected three witnesses to improper questioning, the circuit court properly instructed the jury to disregard the evidence; further, defense counsel made no request for a mistrial, indicating he did not believe the questioning resulted in irreparable prejudice. The admission of the codefendant's guilty plea did not constitute plain error. There was no error in the introduction of the evidence of cocaine in the house and no prejudice to defendant from the introduction of this evidence. The disparity in the codefendant's and defendant's sentencing, which was based on the State's amendment to the indictment, did not violate defendant's constitutional right to trial by jury. Defendant's sentence conformed to the requirements of the habitual offender statute and the circuit court considered defendant's sentence in light of the facts and her previous criminal history. Accordingly, she did not receive a grossly disproportionate sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Perkins v. State


NO. 2008-KA-01387-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


37 So. 3d 656; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 854



December 1, 2009, Decided

Writ of certiorari denied Perkins v. State, 36 So. 3d 455, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 321 (Miss., 2010)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Perkins v. C.M.C.F., 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29019 (N.D. Miss., Mar. 5, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COAHOMA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/24/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. CHARLES E. WEBSTER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF SELLING, TRANSFERRING, OR DELIVERING COCAINE WITHIN 1,500 FEET OF A CHURCH AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO THIRTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Coahoma County Circuit Court, Mississippi of selling, transferring, or delivering cocaine within 1,500 feet of a church in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-142(1) (Rev. 2005). Defendant was sentenced, as a habitual offender, to 30 years in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant asserted that the verdict that was reached was against the overwhelming weight of the evidence and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The court found that defendant's conviction of selling, transferring, or delivering cocaine within 1,500 feet of a church in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-142(1) (Rev. 2005) was not the overwhelming weight of the evidence because there was sufficient evidence in the record to support the jury's finding that the sale took place within 1,500 feet of Calvary Missionary Baptist Church, the jury's verdict was proof that it believed a sale of crack cocaine took place, and the jury acted well within its province, and the record clearly established that the substance that was bought from defendant was placed in an evidence bag, taken to the Mississippi Crime Laboratory for testing, and determined to be crack cocaine. Defendant's trial attorney was not ineffective for failing to object to the court's jury instruction because the instruction fairly announced the law applicable to the facts presented. Thus, there was no basis for the attorney to object.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Neal v. State


NO. 2008-KA-01295-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


27 So. 3d 460; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 774



November 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Neal v. State, 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 57 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 9, 2010)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Application denied by Neal v. State, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 614 (Miss., May 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAMAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/27/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R.I. PRICHARD III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT THE POSSIBILITY OF PAROLE, WITH THE SENTENCE TO RUN CONSECUTIVELY TO THE CURRENT LIFE SENTENCE THE DEFENDANT IS SERVING.
Neal v. State, 687 So. 2d 1180, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 423 (Miss., 1996)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Lamar County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which resentenced him to serve a sentence of life without the possibility of parole pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-107 (Rev. 2007) after vacating his death sentence. He argued that no statute authorized a life sentence without parole, and his sentence violated his right against ex post facto punishment under Miss. Const. art. 3, § 16 and U.S. Const. art. I, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death for capital murder. His case was remanded for a determination of whether or not he was mentally retarded for purposes of Atkins, a United States Supreme Court case holding that the execution of mentally retarded individuals violated the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution. It was determined that defendant was mentally retarded. The State requested that defendant be resentenced to life without parole. Defendant sought to be resentenced to life with the possibility of parole. The court of appeals held that the circuit court correctly applied § 99-19-107 in resentencing defendant. Because defendant's death penalty was found unconstitutional by the United States Supreme Court's ruling in Atkins, the application of § 99-19-107 was appropriate. The statute clearly stated that no one whose death penalty was ruled unconstitutional could receive life with parole. The application of the statute in no way constituted an ex post facto punishment.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the judgment of the circuit court resentencing defendant to life without the possibility of parole.

Clay v. State


NO. 2008-KA-00691-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


20 So. 3d 743; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 696



October 13, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/17/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WALTER BAILEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION OF COCAINE (2.37 GRAMS) AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PROBATION, PAROLE, EARNED TIME, GOOD-TIME CREDIT, REDUCTION OR SUSPENSION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in absentia of possession of approximately 2.37 grams of cocaine, in violation of Mississippi Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (Rev. 2007), and the Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi) enhanced his sentence under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-147 (Rev. 2005) to a term of life imprisonment because he was a habitual offender. Defendant appealed, asserting two claims on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) his life sentence was disproportionate to the crime and constituted cruel and unusual punishment, and (2) the trial court erred in denying his motion for a new trial or, alternatively, for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict because the verdict was against the overwhelming weight of the evidence. Although life imprisonment was a rather severe sentence, the trial court had complete discretion in sentencing as long as it did not exceed the maximum as defined by statute. Because the conviction was defendant's second drug offense, he was subject to twice the maximum sentence or 60 years. As to the denial of his motion for a new trial, the jury heard testimony from two officers that a bag of cocaine was found in the back seat of the vehicle and that defendant was the only passenger in the back seat. Both officers testified that defendant exhibited suspicious behavior before the stop and behaved in a nervous-like manner during the stop, unlike the other persons in the vehicle. Also, a crack pipe and a small amount of cocaine were found on defendant's person during the pat-down search. Sufficient evidence supported the verdict.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Steward v. State


NO. 2008-CP-00902-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


18 So. 3d 895; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 623



September 22, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/06/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment from the Oktibbeha County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief (PCR). Defendatn was convicted of sexual battery and fondling.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that the convictions and sentences resulting from the multi-count indictment were illegal, and that his claim fell within one of the statutory exceptions to the three-year statute of limitations for filing a PCR motion under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5 (Rev. 2007). The circuit court denied the inmate's PCR motion, finding that it was time-barred and did not fall within any of the exceptions in § 99-39-5. The court agreed. The inmate was mistaken regarding his contention that it was illegal for the State to charge more than one count in a single indictment. The inmate was also mistaken in his contention that the fondling charge merged into the sexual battery charge. It was true that the indictment charged that the fondling occurred over a period of time that included the specific date of the sexual battery, but that fact did not mandate that the fondling charge merged into the sexual battery charge. Sexual battery and fondling are separate crimes. Sexual battery requires penetration; fondling does not. Thus, the inmate was neither improperly indicted nor improperly sentenced, and nothing contained in his PCR motion moved it beyond the procedural bar of § 99-39-5.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/19/2007. TRIAL JUDGE:HON. ROBERT WALTER BAILEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF FELONY DRIVING UNDER THE INFLUENCE AND SENTENCED, AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER, TO FIVE YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of felony DUI as a habitual offender pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (2007). The Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi) sentenced him to five years of imprisonment. Defendant appealed, raising five issued, which were recast as (1) whether the circuit court erred in failing to grant his pretrial motion to suppress evidence, and (2) whether he was denied due process during his trial proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's core argument was that the police chief had no authority to stop or arrest him, because he never committed any offense in the chief's jurisdiction. He further argued that his arrest occurred when the pursuit to make the arrest began and that he had not committed any felony at that time. Defendant was arrested after he arrived at his home and got out of his car. At that time, he had committed the crime of felony DUI, as well as the crime of driving with a suspended license. When the police chief began his pursuit, it was not a pursuit for the purpose of making an arrest. Rather, it was a pursuit to give a courtesy warning. Defendant's arrest was legal. Most of defendant's due process claims were subsumed in the larger issue of whether evidence of his DUI should have been suppressed because of his alleged illegal arrest. As to the other issues, they were without merit. There was no reversible error in the trial judge's refusal to recuse himself from hearing posttrial motions.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Davis v. State


NO. 2007-CP-00126-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


17 So. 3d 1149; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 588



September 8, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ADAMS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/11/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LILLIE BLACKMON SANDERS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of uttering a forgery in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-21-59. The Adam County Circuit Court, MS, accepted defendant's plea. Defendant timely filed a motion for postconviction relief, which the circuit court denied. Defendant timely appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the circuit court imposed upon him an unconstitutional and disproportionate sentence. Defendant alleged that the circuit court improperly and unfairly considered other pending charges of uttering that he faced in other jurisdictions when it sentenced him. However, the case law held that in sentencing, the trial court had broad discretion in the things it was able to consider and may appropriately conduct an inquiry broad in scope, largely unlimited as to the kind of information it may consider, or the source from which it may come. In the instant case, the circuit court appeared to largely rely on the fact that defendant engaged in a "malicious scheme" to defraud merchants by using a computer program to create counterfeit checks. Thus, the instant court could not find that the circuit court abused its discretion in considering the pending charges against defendant when it sentenced defendant within the statutory limits provided in Miss. Code Ann. § 97-21-33. Because defendant's sentence fell within the statutory limits proscribed pursuant to § 97-21-33, defendant's sentence did not lead this court to an inference of gross disproportionality.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Simoneaux v. State


NO. 2007-CA-01983-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


29 So. 3d 26; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 445



July 21, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Simoneaux v. State, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 879 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 8, 2009)
Writ of certiorari denied Simoneaux v. State, 29 So. 3d 774, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 115 (Miss., 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Simoneaux v. Mississippi, 562 U.S. 836, 131 S. Ct. 151, 178 L. Ed. 2d 38, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 6093 (2010)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Simoneaux v. State, 2016 Miss. App. LEXIS 292 (Miss. Ct. App., May 10, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/29/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DAVID STRONG, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Pike County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that denied his motion for postconviction relief following his convictions, based upon guilty pleas, of sexual abuse of a vulnerable adult who lived in a nursing home, one count of sexual battery, two burglary-related counts, and two counts of voyeurism, which stemmed from him peeping into nursing homes and spying upon the residents.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, petitioner argued that convicting him of both sexual abuse of a vulnerable adult and sexual battery violated double jeopardy concerns and that the circuit court erred in banishing him from the state after he served his prison terms. On review, the court held that the crime of sexual abuse of a vulnerable adult under Miss. Code Ann. § 43-47-19 (Supp. 2008) did not encompass the crime of sexual battery under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-95 (Rev. 2006), and a conviction of both offenses did not implicate double jeopardy concerns because the crimes required additional and different elements of proof; specifically, the former offense did not require proof of penetration, while the latter offense did require this proof. Additionally, abuse of a vulnerable adult required proof that defendant willfully inflicted physical pain or injury upon a vulnerable adult, while sexual battery had no such requirement. Regarding petitioner's sentence, the court held that, although it appeared from the record that petitioner's banishment from Mississippi was part of an agreed upon sentencing recommendation, the practice of dumping criminals has been held improper on public policy grounds.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the petition for post-conviction relief was modified to strike the banishment provision. As modified, the circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

Brentwood Health Mgmt. of Miss., LLC v. Miss. State Dep't of Health


NO. 2008-SA-00169-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


29 So. 3d 775; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 261



May 19, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Brentwood Health Mgmt. of Miss., LLC v. Miss. State Dep't of Health, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 798 (Miss. Ct. App., Nov. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/17/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DENISE OWENS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED DECISION OF STATE DEPARTMENT OF HEALTH TO REVOKE CERTIFICATES OF NEED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged a decision from the Hinds County Chancery Court, Mississippi, which affirmed a decision from appellee Mississippi State Department of Health (MSDH) revoking two certificates of need (CONs).


OVERVIEW: The CONs were revoked after there was no substantial progress made on two projects. The chancery court found that the MSDH had the authority to revoke the CONs and that its decision was neither arbitrary nor capricious. The hospital sought review. In affirming, the appellate court noted that, even though the Mississippi Legislature had authorized the CONs, this did not mean that the MSDH did not have the power to revoke them. The language in Miss. Code Ann. §§ 47-1-191, 41-7-195 indicated that the Legislature did not intend for the CONs to exist in perpetuity. Further, nothing in § 41-7-195(4) indicated that the Legislature intended to limit the revocation power of the MSDH to only those CONs that were not authorized by statute. Next, even though a hearing officer made a misstatement regarding deference, the hearing officer still fulfilled her obligation to weigh the evidence. The hospital experienced no prejudice based on an attorney general's opinion. Finally, the decision to revoke the CONs was not arbitrary or capricious since the hospital had not done anything that qualified as a commencement of construction or a good faith effort to obligate an approved expenditure.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Lyles v. State


NO. 2007-KA-00993-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


12 So. 3d 532; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 263



May 19, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Lyles v. Mississippi, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 73442 (N.D. Miss., May 28, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/25/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES T. KITCHENS, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF OBTAINING MERCHANDISE VALUED AT $ 100 OR MORE UNDER FALSE PRETENSES AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PAROLE OR PROBATION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Oktibbeha County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of obtaining merchandise valued at $ 100 or more under false pretenses in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-19-55 (Rev. 2000), and which sentenced him as a habitual offender, under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (Rev. 2000) to life imprisonment without eligibility for parole or probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant wrote a bad check to a liquor store. On appeal, the court determined that the testimony of a bank employee that defendant received regular monthly account statements, that defendant's account was closed due to returned checks, and that a few days after the closure defendant would have received an account closure notification was legally sufficient to establish that defendant knew of his negative balance and of the account's closure prior to his writing the bad check. In addition, introduction into evidence of bank statements properly fell under Miss. R. Evid. 404(b) exceptions of knowledge and intent, and under Miss. R. Evid. 403, the evidence was not overly prejudicial as the bank record did not include any information regarding other indictments, it was accompanied by a limiting instruction and the prosecutor did not emphasize any other bounced checks. Finally, the court found that life imprisonment was not constitutionally disproportionate for defendant's conviction as a habitual offender under § 99-19-83 because defendant's criminal history showed that he had an inability to conform his behavior to the requirements that society expected of him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Writ of certiorari dismissed, in part, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Motion denied by, Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part, Motion denied by Whitley v. City of Brandon, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 577 (Miss., Nov. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/14/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DAN H. FAIRLY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: ORDERED LANDOWNER TO ABATE NUISANCE.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city filed a complaint for injunctive relief asking a county court to order appellant property owner to remove offending vehicles from his property. The case was transferred to the Chancery Court of Rankin County, Mississippi, which entered a judgment finding the property owner to be in violation of the city's ordinances and granting an injunction in favor of the city. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: A number of inoperable motor vehicles, in various states of repair, were located on the property owner's property, which had been recently annexed. The appellate court found no violation of the property owner's right to continue his nonconforming use of the land. The property owner next argued that Brandon, Miss., Code of Ordinances § 34-21 was unconstitutionally vague; however, the appellate court found that the ordinance provided a reasonable person an ordinary opportunity to understand the prohibited conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancery court was affirmed.

Knight v. Miss. Transp. Comm'n


NO. 2008-CA-00897-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


10 So. 3d 962; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 217



April 21, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 7, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
TRIAL COURT CALHOUN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/12/2008. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HENRY L. LACKEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MISSISSIPPI TRANSPORTATION COMMISSION IMMUNE FROM SUIT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death suit, appellants, the beneficiaries of two decedents who died in a car accident, challenged summary judgment granted by the Calhoun County Circuit Court (Mississippi) in favor of appellee, the Mississippi Transportation Commission (MTC), arguing that the circuit court erred in concluding that the MTC was immune from liability under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (MTCA), Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-9(1)(d) (Supp. 2008).


OVERVIEW: The decedent's beneficiaries filed suit against the MTC for negligently maintaining a highway and failing to warn of dangerous road conditions. On review of summary judgment granted in favor of the MTC, the court ruled that the MTC was immune from liability under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (MTCA), Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-9(1)(d) (Supp. 2008). Decisions regarding the maintenance and repair of highways and the placement of traffic control devices were discretionary matters entrusted to public officials. Because their decisions involved discretionary functions and not ministerial adherence to established policy or protocol, their discretionary acts were subject to immunity under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-9(1)(d). Further, where any of the immunities enumerated in Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-9(1) (Supp. 2008) applied, the governmental agency was completely immune from the claims arising from its acts or omissions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Jackson v. State


NO. 2007-CP-01470-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


19 So. 3d 106; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 146



March 17, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Jackson v. State, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 651 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PEARL RIVER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/7/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R.I. PRICHARD III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.
Jackson v. State, 872 So. 2d 708, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 402 (Miss. Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Pearl River County Circuit Court (Mississippi) dismissing his motion for post-conviction relief on the ground that it was time-barred by the three-year statute of limitations, under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (Rev. 2007).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to one count of deliberate-design murder and one count of aggravated assault. He was sentenced to life imprisonment for the murder charge and twenty years on the assault charge, with the sentences to run consecutively. A first petition for post-conviction relief was denied, and the denial was affirmed. The trial court summarily dismissed his second petition for post-conviction relief for untimeliness, under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (Rev. 2007). The instant petition was filed nearly six years after his conviction. Defendant failed to raise any arguments that would excepted him from the three-year statute of limitations. Moreover, the court found that the instant petition was barred as a successive writ. Under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-23(6) (Supp. 2008), any order dismissing a prisoner's motion was a final judgment and a bar to a second or successive motion. Defendant also did not raise any statutory exceptions to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-23(6).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Hudson v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


31 So. 3d 1; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 58



February 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Hudson v. State, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 502 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 4, 2009)
Writ of certiorari granted Hudson v. State, 20 So. 3d 680, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 547 (Miss., 2009)
Reversed by Hudson v. State, 30 So. 3d 1199, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 160 (Miss., Mar. 25, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WINSTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/01/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. C.E. MORGAN III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION OF LESS THAN 0.10 GRAM OF COCAINE AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO LIFE IMPRISONMENT IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PAROLE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Winston County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of possession of less than 0.10 gram of cocaine in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(c)(1)(A) (Rev. 2005), and which sentenced him to life imprisonment without eligibility for parole based on his status as a habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (Rev. 2007).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence against him was insufficient to convict him and that his sentence was cruel and unusual. According to defendant, because the amount of cocaine was so insignificant that it could not bee seen with the naked eye and thus, the State failed to show knowledge. A forensic examiner testified that the cocaine testified that she found cocaine in defendant's shirt pocket and in one of pocket of his pants, and that it was visible with the naked eye. The court found that a reasonable fact-finder could infer that defendant possessed the cocaine found in his pockets because it was found in the clothes defendant was wearing when he was arrested. The jury could have reasonably concluded that defendant was wearing his own clothes. Thus, the court found that there was sufficient evidence to convict him. The court determined that defendant's life sentence without parole was mandatory under the circumstances and did not arise solely from his conviction of possession of cocaine but based on his status as a habitual offender. Finally, defendant's claim was procedurally barred because he did not address all three factors of the proportionality analysis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
