Bell v. State


NO. 2007-CP-01857-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


2 So. 3d 747; 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 50



February 3, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PRENTISS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/04/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Prentiss County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed her petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to two separate charges of possession of more than 0.1 gram, but less than 2 grams, of cocaine. Defendant argued that the circuit court erred in dismissing her motion and that she was not procedurally barred from raising the issue of involuntary plea based on new evidence and ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held that the trial court did not err in dismissing the motion because none of the arguments proposed by defendant as grounds for relief fell within the purview of Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(1) (Rev. 2007). Defendant acknowledged that she freely and voluntarily entered a guilty plea to both charges and that she understood the maximum penalty allowed. In addition, the issues of new evidence and ineffective assistance of counsel were procedurally barred from review by the court because they were being raised for the first time in the appeal. Furthermore, defendant's plea would nullify any belief that new evidence would prove that she was wrongfully accused, charged, and sentenced. Finally, considering the dialogue between defendant and the trial judge in her plea colloquy, the court was satisfied that defendant received adequate legal service.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Ellis v. Miss. Baptist Med. Ctr., Inc.


NO. 2007-CA-01315-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


997 So. 2d 996; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 780



December 16, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/24/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MEDICAL MALPRACTICE SUIT DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action, appellant, the executrix of a decedent's estate, challenged a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that granted the motion to dismiss of appellee health care providers, arguing that the circuit court erred in dismissing her lawsuit based upon her failure to a certificate of consultation as required by Mississippi Code Annotated section 11-1-58(1)(a) (Supp. 2008).


OVERVIEW: The executrix commenced a medical malpractice action but failed to file a certificate of consultation stating that her attorney had consulted with a qualified medical expert and concluded that there was a reasonable basis for the action. Based upon the absence of the certificate, the health care providers moved to dismiss. Although the executrix filed a certificate of consultation, the circuit court granted the motion, finding that the certificate was insufficient in failing to set forth that the consultation occurred before the lawsuit was filed. The executrix filed a motion to reconsider, attaching affidavits establishing that the consultation occurred before the lawsuit was filed. The circuit court denied the motion. On review, the court concluded that the circuit court erred in granting the motion to dismiss. Only the statute supreme court had the authority to promulgate rules of procedure; the statute was an unconstitutional procedural statute. A complaint, otherwise properly filed in accordance with the Mississippi Rules of Civil Procedure, could not be dismissed and need not be amended simply because a plaintiff failed to attach a certificate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Hawkins v. Mississippi, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 26951 (N.D. Miss., Mar. 3, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: BOLIVAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/13/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ALBERT B. SMITH III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF ATTEMPTED BURGLARY OF AN AUTOMOBILE AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PAROLE OR PROBATION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Bolivar County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that convicted him of attempted burglary of an automobile, arguing that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on the defense of abandonment, that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction, and that the imposition of a life sentence was excessive under the Eighth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant approached a parked vehicle, rubbed dew off of the vehicle's window, and looked inside. He then went to a second vehicle and broke its window. When the car's alarm sounded, defendant ran to the vehicle in which his accomplice was waiting, and the accomplice drove the pair away. On review of defendant's conviction of attempted burglary of an automobile, the court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on the defense of abandonment. The abandonment instruction was not supported by the evidence because the evidence suggested that the burglary would have been completed if defendant had not been interrupted by the car alarm. Further, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because a police investigator testified that he saw defendant approach a vehicle and look inside before moving onto a second vehicle, looking inside, and breaking its window. In addition, where defendant had previously been convicted of robbery and two charges of burglary, the trial court properly sentenced defendant as a habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (Rev. 2007).


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. HON. JAMES T. KITCHENS, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Oktibbeha County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of two counts of aggravated assault of law enforcement officers under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-7 and sentencing him to two consecutive sentences of 20 years each.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for nearly striking two officers during a police chase. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by allowing the State to amend the indictments as the amendments eliminated the language alleging any overt act by defendant's attempt to cause bodily harm to the officers, and therefore, because the amendments resulted in substantially defective indictments, defendant's convictions were reversed. The court held that the trial court also erred by refusing to give a lesser non-included offense jury instruction of reckless driving under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-3-1201 (Rev. 2004) because, taking the evidence in the light most favorable to defendant and based on defendant's testimony, the jury could have found that, rather than attempting to hit one officer with his car, he was merely attempting to avoid running into another officer's vehicle, and that defendant went into another officer's lane to allow more room for a car that had pulled over to the right side of the road and that he did not attempt to hit the officer's car or run him off the road. However, the trial court did not err by refusing to instruct the jury on simple assault.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Writ of certiorari denied Williams v. State, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 135 (Miss., Mar. 26, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/10/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK G. VOLLOR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION OF MORE THAN TEN GRAMS BUT LESS THAN THIRTY GRAMS OF COCAINE AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO TWENTY-FOUR YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITHOUT ELIGIBILITY FOR PAROLE OR PROBATION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Warren County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of the possession of cocaine, more then 10 grams, but less than 30 grams, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(c)(1)(D) (Rev. 2005).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed after he was convicted of the possession of cocaine, more than 10 grams, but less than 30 grams. The appellate court affirmed, stating that he was not denied his right to a speedy trial under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Miss. Const. art. 3, § 26. He was aware of the possibility that charges would be brought against him as a result of his arrest and he did not seek any resolution of the charges until after he was served with the indictment in June 2006. Additionally, there was no actual prejudice to defendant as a result of the delay between arrest and trial. The State did not lack jurisdiction to prosecute the charge against defendant even though he was arrested on property owned by the United States because the State was free to enforce its criminal and civil laws on federal land as long as those laws did not conflict with federal law. Thus, the State had jurisdiction to arrest defendant and bring him to trial. Though defendant's sentence might have seemed harsh in light of the sentences received by others convicted of drug possession, his sentence fit within the statutory maximum under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (Rev. 2007).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gray v. State


NO. 2006-CP-01139-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


13 So. 3d 283; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 611



October 7, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Gray v. State, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 178 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 31, 2009)
Writ of certiorari denied Gray v. State, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 344 (Miss., July 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAMAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 6/16/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R.I. PRICHARD III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner appealed a judgment of the Lamar County Circuit Court, Mississippi, which dismissed his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: In October 2004, the prisoner pleaded guilty to the crime of sale and transfer of cocaine. He was sentenced to 15 years in the custody of the Department of Corrections with seven years to serve and eight years suspended. At the time the prisoner committed his crime, offenders convicted of sale or transfer of a controlled substance were eligible to be placed in trusty status and to accumulate trusty-earned time pursuant to former Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-138.1 (Rev. 2001). However, prior to the time he was convicted and sentenced, the statute was amended to exclude offenders convicted of sale or transfer of a controlled substance from eligibility for the earned-time allowance. The effective date of the amendment was April 28, 2004. The instant court concluded that the trial court erred in summarily dismissing the prisoner's motion. An evidentiary hearing was necessary to decide whether application of the amended statute in this case constituted an ex post facto violation. In order to show an ex post facto violation, the prisoner would have to demonstrate that application of the amended statute to him created a sufficient risk of increasing the measure of punishment for his crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Parker v. State


NO. 2007-KA-00490-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


5 So. 3d 458; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 580



September 23, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Parker v. State, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 11 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 6, 2009)

Writ of certiorari denied Parker v. State, 11 So. 3d 1250, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 131 (Miss., 2009)
Related proceeding at, Post-conviction relief denied at Parker v. State, 2017 Miss. App. LEXIS 12 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 10, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/17/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES T. KITCHENS, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF COUNT I, SALE OF COCAINE, AND SENTENCE OF TWENTY YEARS, AND COUNT II, SALE OF COCAINE, AND SENTENCE OF FOURTEEN YEARS TO RUN CONSECUTIVELY TO THE SENTENCE IN COUNT I, ALL IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS, AND A FINE OF $ 10,000.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lowndes County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of two counts of the sale of cocaine and sentenced him to serve twenty years on Count I and fourteen years on Count II, to run consecutively, the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the circuit court erred in refusing to sever Counts I and II of his indictment; in refusing to grant a continuance and to grant one of his peremptory challenges during jury selection; in refusing to grant a mistrial; and his sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The appellate court found that the circuit court did not err in refusing to sever Counts I and II of the indictment as they were separated by only one day, the alleged crimes were the same, and they involved substantially the same facts and witnesses. Manifest injustice did not result from the denial of defendant's motion for a continuance. The State made a sufficient prima facie showing that race was a possible criteria in the defense counsel's exercise of peremptory challenges. The reasons proffered by the defense attorney were not merely pretextual under Batson. Where the prosecutor mistakenly asked an improper question, the circuit judge took appropriate remedial steps, and defendant's motion for mistrial was properly denied. Defendant offered no support for his argument that consecutive sentences for drug offenses within the statutory limits were grossly disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Watts v. State


NO. 2007-CP-00708-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


1 So. 3d 886; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 397



July 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Watts v. State, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 663 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 28, 2008)
Writ of certiorari dismissed Watts v. State, 999 So. 2d 852, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 33 (Miss., 2009)
Writ of certiorari denied Watts v. State, 999 So. 2d 1280, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 16 (Miss., 2009)
Post-conviction proceeding at Watts v. Brewer, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 124866 (S.D. Miss., Sept. 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/12/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT B. HELFRICH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DISMISSED MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After pleading guilty to being an habitual offender for the sale of cocaine, appellant movant received a 30-year sentence. The movant's sentence was suspended, provided that he comply with several conditions. The movant did not comply, and his suspended sentence was revoked. The Forrest County Circuit Court, Mississippi, dismissed the movant's request for post-conviction relief. Aggrieved, the movant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court ordered the movant to leave Hattiesburg as a condition of the suspended sentence. On appeal, the movant asserted the following: (1) the circuit court erred by imposing the conditions of the suspended sentence without first placing him on probation under the supervision of the Mississippi Department of Corrections; (2) the banishment was unenforceable and illegal; (3) the 30-year banishment was unconstitutional. Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-33(1) (Rev. 2004) did not prohibit felons from receiving suspension and then being placed on probation. The conditions placed on the movant's suspended sentence did not equate to the movant being placed on probation. Further, the movant was not entitled to any relief because he suffered no injury or prejudice from receiving a lawful, yet lenient, sentence. As to whether the movant received ineffective assistance of counsel, the movant had acknowledged during his guilty plea proceeding that he was satisfied with the advice he received and the help his attorney had provided. Also, even if the movant's claim of deficient performance were supported by evidence, the movant failed to present any evidence that the movant was prejudiced.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court dismissing the motion for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

Riley v. State


NO. 2007-KA-00445-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


1 So. 3d 877; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 378



June 24, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Riley v. State, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 650 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 14, 2008)
Writ of certiorari denied Riley v. State, 999 So. 2d 1280, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 18 (Miss., Feb. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ATTALA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/6/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOSEPH H. LOPER, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF TWO COUNTS OF TRAFFICKING IN STOLEN FIREARMS AND SENTENCED TO SERVE TWO CONCURRENT TERMS OF THIRTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Attala County Circuit Court (Mississippi) found defendant guilty of two counts of trafficking in stolen firearms under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-35(3)(c) (Rev. 2006), but acquitted him on all three counts of burglary. He was sentenced to serve two concurrent 30-year sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-35(3)(c) (Rev. 2006) was unconstitutional, but his constitutional attacks on Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-35 were procedurally barred because the issues he presented were not previously raised before the trial court. In addition, defendant's conviction was not against the overwhelming weight of the evidence because the accomplice's testimony was reasonable, consistent, and substantially uncontradicted. Furthermore, the jury received a cautionary instruction relating to the manner in which the accomplice testimony should be viewed. Additionally, the accomplice's testimony that defendant knew the firearms were stolen was corroborated because defendant told the investigators that he had nothing to do with the burglaries and only pointed out places where guns were sold. Moreover, one of the buyers testified that defendant sold the guns to him. Also, under the Eighth Amendment, defendant's 30-year sentence for each offense was not unconstitutionally disproportionate to his crime as it was within the statutory guidelines, was below the potential life sentence he could have received, and was not grossly disproportionate to the crime he committed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Dobbs v. State


NO. 2007-CP-00900-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


6 So. 3d 1088; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 354



June 10, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing dismissed by, En banc Dobbs v. State, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 688 (Miss. Ct. App., Nov. 12, 2008)
Writ of certiorari granted Dobbs v. State, 999 So. 2d 852, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 28 (Miss., 2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by Dennis Dobbs v. Miss., 6 So. 3d 1085, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 165 (Miss., Apr. 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARSHALL COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/10/2007. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW K. HOWORTH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In addressing appellant inmate's various filings, the Marshall County Circuit Court (Mississippi) treated them as a motion for post-conviction relief and denied relief to appellant. On appeal, he claimed that his motions were not post-conviction motions and instead, they were complaints under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: In his filings, appellant alleged that he was housed in inhuman conditions, e.g., the windows of the facility would not open, there were no air conditioners installed, and the facility lacked a fire sprinkler system, thereby creating a fire hazard. His allegations did not fall under any of the grounds for post-conviction relief enumerated in Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(1). Therefore, he was not entitled to any relief under the post-conviction statute. Because the circuit court treated the filings as a motion for post-conviction relief, it was proper to deny relief. Appellant's attempt to assert a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was without merit because he never filed any such complaint or any corresponding summons; he only filed various motions and documents. Under Miss. R. Civ. P. 3(a), a party had to file a complaint to institute an action. Whether appellant properly asserted grounds sufficient to warrant relief under § 1983 was irrelevant because he did not file a complaint asserting those grounds. Moreover, appellant filed his motion against the State and the State could not be sued under § 1983 in state court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

RESTITUTION TO BE PAID JOINTLY AND SEVERALLY BY CO-DEFENDANTS. DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED: 8/07/2007. MOTION FOR REHEARING FILED: 9/12/2007-GRANTED.
Salts v. State, 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 513 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 7, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in the Lee County Circuit Court of four counts of embezzlement and sentenced to a total of ten years each in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections and an $ 11,000 fine. Defendants were also ordered to pay restitution. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by failing to grant a continuance to allow defendants' attorney to prepare for trial after he took the case a few days before trial was set to begin. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendants presented no concrete facts to demonstrate any prejudice against them. Although the attorney had a limited amount of time to interview witnesses and review the admittedly large amount of documents in the case, defendants presented no evidence that the lack of time had any impact on their case. They pointed to no particular witness whose questioning might have made a difference, nor did they indicate that there was anything in the documents that could have been discovered had the attorney had more time to review the case. In the absence of any showing of prejudice, defendants failed to show that the trial court abused its discretion in failing to grant them a last-minute continuance, especially in light of the fact that five continuances had already been granted to the defense over the course of almost a year and a half. Therefore, the trial court properly denied defendants' motion for a continuance.


OUTCOME: The orders of restitution were reversed and remanded for further consideration. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Jones v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


976 So. 2d 407; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 120

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate challenged a decision from the Monroe County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed his motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate entered a guilty plea to one count of simple assault on an officer. A suspended sentence imposed was revoked. The trial court dismissed an application for post-conviction relief, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the inmate failed to establish that he received ineffective assistance of counsel under the Strickland test. In addition, the inmate failed to include a sworn affidavit to support his claim or explain why it was not include with his post-conviction motion, as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-9(1) (2007). Next, there was a factual basis for the plea given the inmate's admission. An evidentiary hearing was not required under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-11(2) (Rev. 2000). There was no indication that the inmate's mental capabilities were at issue; he failed to demonstrate that the was incapable of making a rational defense. Moreover, the inmate was able to answer all question and testify during the plea hearing. There was no error in finding a violation of the terms of supervision, the inmate was not entitled to an attorney at the revocation proceeding, and the sentence was not cruel and unusual under the Eighth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Staten v. State


NO. 2006-KA-01612-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


989 So. 2d 938; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 76



January 29, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Staten v. State, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 297 (Miss. Ct. App., May 20, 2008)
Writ of certiorari denied Staten v. State, 993 So. 2d 832, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 400 (Miss., Aug. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GRENADA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/3/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. C. E. MORGAN, III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Grenada County Circuit Court (Mississippi) found defendant guilty of murder under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(1) (Rev. 2006). The trial court sentenced him to life in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted he was the only adult at home with the victim that day. Also, the evidence of the bloody T-shirt, the bloody piece of the crutch and stopper, and the numerous circular injuries on the victim's body from another piece of the crutch strongly suggested that defendant beat the victim severely with a crutch. In addition, the evidence showed that the crutch broke into pieces, and that defendant disposed of the pieces, but that he overlooked the two pieces found by the police. Additionally, defendant's actions of beating and strangling the victim were willful acts likely to cause death or serious bodily injury and evinced a reckless indifference to the danger to human life from which malice could be inferred. Furthermore, defendant's expressions of unfamiliarity with the basics of cardiopulmonary resuscitation (CPR) while possessing certification in CPR and first aid training were inconsistent with his innocence of murder. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of murder. Also, under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-21 (Rev. 2006), defendant was convicted of only murder and was properly sentenced to life imprisonment, not to life without the possibility of parole.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Colburn v. State


NO. 2005-KA-01882-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


990 So. 2d 206; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 74



January 29, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Colburn v. State, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 340 (Miss. Ct. App., June 3, 2008)
En banc, Writ of certiorari denied Colburn v. State, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 472 (Miss., Sept. 11, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/5/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW K. HOWORTH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF MURDER AND SENTENCE OF LIFE IN PRISON IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Chicksaw County Circuit Court (Mississippi) found defendant not guilty of capital murder under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e) (Rev. 2000), but found him guilty of simple murder under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(1)(a) (Rev. 2006). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motions for a directed verdict or a judgment notwithstanding the verdict because there was evidence of (1) three confessions made by defendant in the presence of three different individuals; (2) a strained relationship between defendant and the victim; (3) defendant's dislike for her job as a live-in-caretaker and the victim; and (4) the victim's autopsy showed he did not die of natural causes because he was alive when the fire started. Thus, there was sufficient proof presented at trial to establish the essential elements of murder. In addition, regarding defendant's motion for a new trial, her argument centered around her contention that there was no evidence that she caused the fire, thereby causing the victim's death; however, because of the many inconsistencies in the various statements of what happened the night of the fire, not to mention defendant's confessions, allowing the verdict to stand did not sanction an unconscionable injustice. Therefore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a new trial. Finally, the trial court did not err in accepting a verdict of guilty of murder.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Booker v. State


NO. 2004-KA-02143-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


5 So. 3d 411; 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 77



January 29, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted Booker v. State, 981 So. 2d 298, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 211 (Miss., 2008)
Affirmed by Booker v. State, 5 So. 3d 356, 2008 Miss. LEXIS 519 (Miss., Oct. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/20/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DALE HARKEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER. SENTENCED TO LIFE IMPRISONMENT WITHOUT POSSIBILITY OF PAROLE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS. DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED - 08/29/2006. MOTION FOR REHEARING FILED: 09/26/2006-DENIED.
Booker v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 635 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 29, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of capital murder and sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his confession should not have been admitted because his statements were the result of promises from the officers and were given because of his limited learning capacity. The court of appeals disagreed. After signing a "waiver of rights" form read to him by officers, defendant described the events leading up to the victim's death. During the suppression hearing, defendant testified that the officer promised him treatment as a youthful offender if he told the truth about what happened to the victim. However, officers all testified that defendant gave his confession voluntarily, and he was not promised anything for his truthfulness. After questions arose about defendant's limited learning capacity, all three again testified that defendant did not seem to have any problems understanding his rights, and he signed the waiver of rights form willingly after his rights were read to him. At the hearing, defendant was able to read aloud for the trial court each right listed on the waiver. Although he claimed to not remember where he lived, or any of his teachers' names, defendant acknowledged initialing the waiver in front of the officers.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Brown v. State


NO. 2006-KA-00717-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


970 So. 2d 1300; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 826



December 11, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/10/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL M. TAYLOR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF MANSLAUGHTER AND SENTENCED TO TWENTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITH FOUR YEARS SUSPENDED AND FOUR YEARS OF POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Pike County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted her of manslaughter and sentenced her to 20 years in custody, four years suspended, and four years of post-release supervision.


OVERVIEW: A witness confirmed defendant's story that a victim committed suicide, but the witness later recanted this statement and implicated defendant. Defendant was convicted, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court held that there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-35 (Rev. 2006) or Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-47 (Rev. 2006). The evidence included the murder weapon, the eyewitness testimony, the testimony of police, and the conclusions of the coroner and the doctor who performed the autopsy. Due to the direct testimony of the eyewitness, there was no need to give a circumstantial evidence instruction. The State did not introduce evidence of prior bad acts under Miss. R. Evid. 404(b). There was probable cause to arrest defendant for the crime. The appellate court was unable to review alleged errors relating to jury instructions due to a failure to comply with Miss. R. App. P. 28(a)(6). Alleged torture did not justify the dismissal of the charges, defendant was not incompetent under Miss. Unif. Cir. & Cty. R. 9.06, no jurors saw defendant in shackles, and the issue of cruel and unusual punishment was not raised to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Bessent v. Clark


NO. 2005-CP-01083-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


974 So. 2d 928; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 633



September 25, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 13, 2008.
Rehearing denied by, En banc Bessent v. Clark, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 25 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/12/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM H. SINGLETARY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT GRANTED DEFENDANTS' MOTION TO DISMISS.
Bessent v. State, 808 So. 2d 979, 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 358 (Miss. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Rankin County Chancery Court, Mississippi, convicted appellant inmate of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. The circuit court sentenced the inmate to twenty-five years in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections. The appellate court affirmed the circuit court. The inmate's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 complaint in the Hinds County Chancery Court was dismissed. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that to the extent that the inmate sought his freedom through a collateral attack on his conviction, his complaint had to be viewed as an action under the Post-Conviciton Collateral Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-1 et seq. (Rev. 2000). To the extent that the inmate sought damages against state entities, officials, and employees, his complaint had to be viewed as an action under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-1 (Rev. 2002). Because the appellate court affirmed the inmate's conviction on direct appeal, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-7 mandated that he obtain permission from the supreme court to seek post-conviction relief from the trial court. He failed to do so. The chancery court lacked jurisdiction to entertain his collateral attacks and the appellate court lacked jurisdiction to entertain his appeal. Those governmental entities and employees were immune from the inmate's lawsuit as he was incarcerated when he filed his complaint. The inmate could not sue the various officials based on the constitutionality of his arrest under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 as his conviction had not been invalidated. The inmate's appeal was frivolous.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

390 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Morgan v. State


NO. 2006-CP-01644-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


966 So. 2d 204; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 545



August 28, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MONROE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/30/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SHARION R. AYCOCK. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to a charge of sale of cocaine under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(b)(1) and was sentenced to serve 30 years' imprisonment with 15 years suspended. The Monroe County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Concluding that defendant's allegations of error contained no merit, the court held that: (1) defendant's allegation that he was subject to an excessive sentence was founded on his mistaken belief that he should have been sentenced for mere possession of cocaine under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(c); (2) Miss. Code Ann.§ 41-29-139 was not unconstitutionally ambiguous because a person of ordinary intelligence would understand that one could be subject to up to 30 years' imprisonment for the sale of cocaine; (3) none of various alleged flaws in the indictment rendered it defective because some of these flaws, such as failure to include a sworn affidavit by the foreman of the grand jury, were waived by the guilty plea, while others, such as failure to contain the amount of cocaine sold, were not legal defects; (4) defendant's allegation that he was threatened with 20 years' imprisonment, a punishment below the maximum, if he did not enter a plea of guilty did not make the guilty plea involuntary; and (5) because the sentence was within the statutory maximum for the sale of cocaine and the indictment was not defective, defendant could not demonstrate that his counsel was ineffective.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Salts v. State


NO. 2006-KA-00437-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 513



August 7, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing granted by, Remanded by Salts v. State, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 199 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 2/21/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER, III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF EMBEZZLEMENT IN COUNT I AND SENTENCED TO FIVE YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS; CONVICTED OF MISDEMEANOR EMBEZZLEMENT IN COUNT IV AND SENTENCED TO SIX MONTHS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE PRENTISS COUNTY SHERIFF'S DEPARTMENT; CONVICTED OF EMBEZZLEMENT IN COUNT V AND SENTENCED TO FIVE YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS; AND CONVICTED OF EMBEZZLEMENT IN COUNT VI AND SENTENCED TO FIVE YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS. THE SENTENCE IN COUNT I IS TO RUN CONSECUTIVE TO THE SENTENCE IN COUNT V, AND CONCURRENT WITH THE SENTENCES IN COUNTS IV AND VI. THE SENTENCE IN COUNT IV IS TO RUN CONCURRENT WITH THE SENTENCES IN COUNTS I, V, AND VI. THE SENTENCE IN COUNT V IS TO RUN CONSECUTIVE TO THE SENTENCE IN COUNT I, AND CONCURRENT WITH THE SENTENCES IN COUNTS IV AND VI. THE SENTENCE IN COUNT VI IS TO RUN CONCURRENT WITH THE SENTENCES IMPOSED IN COUNTS I, IV, AND V. DEFENDANTS ALSO ORDERED TO PAY A $ 10,000 FINE IN COUNT I AND A 1,000 FINE IN COUNT IV.  [*2] RESTITUTION ALSO ORDERED IN THE AMOUNT OF $ 272. 14 TO PAULA COX, $ 216. 07 TO JANETTE TAYLOR, $ 254. 57 TO CHARLES CLARA SIMMONS, AND $ 285. 58 TO SARAH & JAMES MCGEE. RESTITUTION IS TO BE PAID JOINTLY AND SEVERALLY BY CO-DEFENDANTS.
Salts v. Gulf Nat'l Life Ins. Co., 872 So. 2d 667, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 491 (Miss., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED AS FOLLOWS: THE CONVICTION OF EMBEZZLEMENT IN COUNT I; THE CONVICTION OF MISDEMEANOR EMBEZZLEMENT IN COUNT IV AND SENTENCE OF SIX MONTHS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE PRENTISS COUNTY SHERIFF'S DEPARTMENT AND FINE OF $ 1,000; THE CONVICTION OF EMBEZZLEMENT IN COUNT V; AND THE CONVICTION OF EMBEZZLEMENT IN COUNT VI ARE AFFIRMED, BUT THE SENTENCES IN COUNTS I, V, AND VI ARE VACATED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. FURTHERMORE, THE ORDERS OF RESTITUTION ARE REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted, before the Lee County Circuit Court, Mississippi, of embezzlement. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants owned and operated a funeral home. For many years, defendants used an insurer to provide funeral insurance for their customers. The insurer terminated its relationship with defendants; however, many of defendants' clients continued to send their payments to defendants. On appeal, defendants alleged, inter alia, that: (1) they were denied effective representation; (2.) they were never addressed as to a conflict of interest; (3) the trial court erred in not declaring a mistrial. The appellate court rejected the contentions. The fact that new counsel only a few days before trial did not entitle defendants to a continuance. As to the alleged conflict of interest, there was no actual conflict of interest present. There were three distinct incidents about alleged prosecutorial misconduct; however, the issue was without merit. The trial court did err, however, in sentencing the defendants when Miss. Code Ann. § 97-23-19 proscribed the same conduct but provided more lenient punishment. The trial court also erred in ordering defendants to pay restitution to the policyholders because the policyholders who benefitted from the restitution lost nothing as a result of the misconduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, as to the convictions. The matter was reversed and remanded as to the sentences. The sentences were vacated and the orders of restitution were reversed and remanded for further consideration consistent with the opinion.

Jefferson v. State


NO. 2006-CP-00492-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


958 So. 2d 1276; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 440



June 26, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/10/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL R. EUBANKS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: DISMISSAL OF PETITION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF AFFIRMED; JUDGMENT OF SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the Marion County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief (PCR).


OVERVIEW: The inmate entered a guilty plea to one count of uttering forgery. He was sentenced to house arrest, but was placed into custody for the remainder of his 15-year sentence after violating the conditions of the alternative placement. His later motion for PCR relief was dismissed, and this appeal followed. In affirming the dismissal of the PCR motion, the appellate court decided to consider the case, even though it was untimely under Miss. R. App. P. 4(a). Next, although the portion of the sentence relating to house arrest was illegal under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-1003 (Rev. 2004) due to the inmate's prior record, there was no reversible error since the inmate received the benefitted from such. Moreover, the inmate did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel because he was correctly advised of the maximum sentence under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-21-33 (Supp. 2003). Even though the issue was not raised by the inmate, the appellate court found that an illegal sentence was imposed in excess of the 10-year maximum. Therefore, the case was remanded for resentencing for a term not longer than 10 years.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the PCR motion was affirmed. The sentence from the underlying conviction was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

White v. State


NO. 2006-KA-00244-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


958 So. 2d 290; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 412



June 12, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LINCOLN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/19/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL M. TAYLOR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF AGGRAVATED ASSAULT AND SENTENCED TO FIFTEEN YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS, WITH TEN YEARS TO SERVE, FIVE YEARS SUSPENDED AND FIVE YEARS' POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION, TO PAY A FINE OF $ 2,500 AND TO PAY $ 4,639. 81 IN RESTITUTION TO THE CRIME VICTIMS' COMPENSATION FUND.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Lincoln County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted her of aggravated assault in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-7(2) (Rev. 2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of aggravated assault upon the victim, whom she had cut across his chest and upper right arm during an altercation at the victim's home. On appeal, the court affirmed, stating that the evidence supported the conviction. The victim testified that defendant swung at him and that he was bleeding as a result. Additionally, another witness testified that he observed defendant and the victim argue and saw a "hand motion" from defendant during the argument. Afterwards, the victim stated that defendant had cut him. Defendant was sentenced to 15 years, with 10 to serve and 5 years of post-release supervision. The appellate court affirmed that sentence, stating that it was not grossly disproportionate to the crime committed. The sentence was well within the statutory guidelines set forth in Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-7(2) (Rev. 2006) and the trial court noted that aggravated assault was a serious crime. The trial court also considered the fact that defendant had a relatively clean record, with no prior felony convictions, and that defendant had been consistently employed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment and assessed all costs of the appeal to defendant.

Bridges v. State


NO. 2006-CP-00110-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


973 So. 2d 246; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 240



April 17, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Bridges v. State, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 22 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/8/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BEVERLEY MITCHELL FRANKLIN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed his motion for post-conviction relief (PCR).


OVERVIEW: The inmate entered a guilty plea to possession of methamphetamine precursors as a prior drug offender. The agreement provided that the inmate was to be sentenced as a second and subsequent drug offender. He was sentenced to 34 years in prison. The trial court dismissed a request for PCR, and an appeal was filed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the guilty plea was entered knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently. The record showed that the inmate was informed of the consequences of the plea by the trial court. Even if his attorney suggested that he might receive a sentence of 8 to 12 years, this prediction did not render the plea involuntary. Moreover, the sentence imposed was not disproportionate since it was within the statutory limitations in Miss. Code Ann. §§ 41-29-313, 41-29-147 (Rev. 2005). By pleading guilty, the inmate waived his claims relating to calling witnesses during his suppression hearing and the right to a speedy trial. The inmate was not denied effective assistance of counsel under the Sixth Amendment since he failed to make such an assertion during the plea and sentencing hearings. Finally, he was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Westbrook v. State


NO. 2006-CP-01207-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


953 So. 2d 286; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 199



April 3, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari dismissed Westbrook v. State, 962 So. 2d 38, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 436 (Miss., 2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Westbrook v. Kelly, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 119522 (N.D. Miss., Apr. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MONROE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/8/2006. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SHARION R. AYCOCK. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF - DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Monroe County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of the sale of cocaine after defendant entered a plea of guilty to the charge. He was sentenced to twenty years in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections with ten years suspended and five years' post-release supervision. The trial court denied his motion for post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentence exceeded the statutorily prescribed penalty. The appellate court noted that his sentence of twenty years with ten suspended and five years post-release suspension was within the zero to thirty year limits of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(c). Although defendant argued that the statute was ambiguous because he believed Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(b) conflicted with § 41-29-139(c), he was convicted under the subsection that criminalized the sale of a controlled substance, while § 41-29-139(c) proscribed possession of a controlled substance. They were two different provisions dealing with two different situations. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague as a person of ordinary intelligence would understand by reading Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(b) that he could face significant prison time for selling cocaine. The sale of controlled substances did not infringe on any of defendant's constitutionally protected rights. The issues concerning the alleged defects in the indictment were without merit. The claims defendant argued to be defects in the indictment were insufficient to show deficiency in his counsel's performance or prejudice to his case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Jackson v. State


NO. 2004-KA-01460-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


962 So. 2d 649; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 104



February 27, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Jackson v. State, 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 380 (Miss. Ct. App., May 29, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied Jackson v. State, 962 So. 2d 38, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 434 (Miss., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: AMITE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 2/12/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF SALE OF MARIJUANA WITHIN A CORRECTIONAL FACILITY AND SENTENCED TO THREE YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS, FINE OF $ 25,000 AND DISBARMENT.
Miss. Bar v. Jackson, 904 So. 2d 109, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1340 (Miss., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Amite County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of the sale of marijuana within a correctional facility in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-198(1). Defendant, an attorney, was further disbarred under Miss. Code Ann. § 73-3-41 (Rev. 2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an attorney, was convicted of the sale of marijuana within a corrections facility and was sentenced to three years in the Department of Corrections. He was also ordered to pay a fine and court costs and he was disbarred. The appellate court affirmed, stating that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The presence of direct evidence meant that his case was not a circumstantial evidence case. And, it was in the context of the issuance of search warrants that a confidential informant must be proven reliable. Defendant's client did not supply information to obtain a search warrant. Instead, the client cooperated with authorities during the equivalent of a sting operation. The judge in the trial did not need to recuse himself because nothing in the judge's response gave rise to overcome the presumption of impartiality. Defendant only speculated that the judge could not have been impartial. The denial of defendant's motion for a change of venue was rightfully denied because the impaneled jury members all stated that they would serve as fair and impartial jurors. The denial of an accomplice instruction was proper because the client was not an accomplice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bacon v. State


NO. 2005-KA-01057-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


950 So. 2d 250; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 117



February 27, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEAKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/12/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF FLEEING A LAW OFFICER IN A MOTOR VEHICLE AND SENTENCED TO THREE YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AND TO PAY A FINE OF $ 1,500.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Leake County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of fleeing a law officer in a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: An officer suspected that defendant was intoxicated after observing his driving. When the officer tried to pull the vehicle over by use of his siren and blue lights, defendant sped off at a high rate of speed. Defendant traveled over the center line and forced two other vehicles to pull off the highway. Defendant was found guilty, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the indictment included every essential element of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-9-72(2) (Rev. 2006). The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that he should have been charged with a misdemeanor instead under § 97-9-72(1). The indictment successfully alleged that, after defendant was signalled to stop, he continued to operate his motor vehicle with a reckless disregard for the safety of others. Next, the indictment did not have to allege that defendant was guilty of an underlying crime because the crime of fleeing a law officer in a motor vehicle was not predicated on another. Finally, defendant's argument that § 97-9-72(2) was void for vagueness was not considered since it was raised for the first time on review.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Adams v. State


NO. 2005-CP-01761-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


962 So. 2d 640; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 38



February 6, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Adams v. State, 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 614 (Miss. Ct. App., May 22, 2007)
En banc, Rehearing denied by Adams v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 464 (Miss., Aug. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/18/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LARRY EUGENE ROBERTS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate entered a guilty plea to a second degree burglary charge. A subsequent "notice of post-conviction relief" was denied, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court held there was no procedure for filing a "notice" for post-conviction relief; the filing clearly stated that the document was a motion. Next, the trial court was not required to return the filing to the inmate under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-9(4) (Supp. 2006). The motion did not contain a concise statement of the statement or grounds upon which the motion was based, as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-9(1)(c) (Supp. 2006), nor did it state a claim upon which relief could have been granted under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(1) (Supp. 2006). The determination of whether to return the motion to the inmate was left to the trial court since it did not comply with the statutory requirements. Further, the inmate was not prejudiced by the forfeiture of earned time under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-138 (Supp. 2006) because he was unable to earn such as a habitual offender. Finally, there was no evidence that the judge in the case should have recused himself based on a comment about the proceeding being a "sham."


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Smith v. State


NO. 2005-CP-01700-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


963 So. 2d 1168; 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 39



February 6, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing, en banc, denied by Smith v. State, 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 384 (Miss. Ct. App., May 29, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied, En banc Smith v. State, 964 So. 2d 508, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 499 (Miss., Sept. 6, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Sunflower County (Mississippi), which denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: In 1995, defendant entered guilty pleas to several different drug and weapon charges. He was sentenced as a habitual offender pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (Rev. 2000), based on four prior felony convictions. More than nine years later, in 2004, defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief, asserting that the habitual offender statute under which he was sentenced was unconstitutional because it did not require a jury trial to determine whether an offender met the eligibility requirements for enhanced punishment. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court found defendant's argument unavailing, as his assertions were based on a misperception of the law. Defendant had no entitlement to a jury trial on the issue of whether or not he qualified for enhanced punishment under the habitual offender statute. Defendant failed to prove that an intervening decision of the United States Supreme Court or the Mississippi Supreme Court excepted the procedural time bar of his claim pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (Supp. 2006).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Family Dollar Stores of Miss., Inc. v. Montgomery


NO. 2005-CA-00126-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


946 So. 2d 426; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 929



December 12, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JEFFERSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/27/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LAMAR PICKARD. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT FOR MONTGOMERY FOR $ 211,786. 28. APPORTIONED TO FAMILY DOLLAR FIFTY PERCENT, BOWMAN THIRTY PERCENT, TURNER TWENTY PERCENT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant and cross-appellee lessee, a corporation, challenged a judgment of the Jefferson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which entered an order finding the lessee comparatively liable, together with defendant general contractor and a subcontractor, for personal injuries to the lessee's employees and patrons. Appellee and cross-appellant lessor appealed on the amount of damages awarded for injury to his property.


OVERVIEW: The lessee ran a store. Pursuant to the lease, the lessee was to have renovations made in a workmanlike manner. The lessee contracted with a general contractor for the work, and the general contractor contracted with a subcontractor for removal of a wall. The roof partially collapsed during the removal of the wall, injuring some of the lessee's employees and patrons. The lessee settled the personal injury claims. Subsequently, the lessor sued the lessee for breach of contract and the general contractor for negligence. The trial court apportioned liability, finding the lessee 50 percent at fault, the general contractor 30 percent at fault, and the subcontractor 20 percent at fault under Miss. Code Ann. § 85-5-7 (Supp. 2006). In reversing, the court held that the trial court had improperly found that the lessee negligently performed its duties as architect because the contract was silent as to the duties of an architect and, absent a delineation of such duties, no duty to warn could be imputed to the lessee. The court held that the trial court's damages calculation was sustainable but that it might also be proper to further evaluate the damage award, if appropriate, on remand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.
